God's Writing: Descriptive, Not Prescriptive
Explains divine writing is descriptive, not a command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between God's writing as a description of what will happen and as a command that would necessitate immediate existence.

Core Idea
God's writing describes the future; it does not command it.

In this passage from the commentary on al-Fiqh al-Akbar, the author unpacks a key phrase about divine decree. He clarifies that when God writes in the Preserved Tablet, He is describing what will occur according to His eternal knowledge and decree, not issuing a command that would force immediate creation. This distinction preserves both God's timeless knowledge and the temporal nature of events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of the flow. Notice the word-by-word gloss of the original phrase.
2
Identify the main doctrinal point
Look for the sentence that begins 'ولكن كتبه بالوصف لا بالحكم'. This is the core thesis: God's writing is descriptive, not prescriptive.
The author contrasts 'wasf' (description) with 'hukm' (command).
3
Understand the criticism of the commentator
The author rejects a commentator who said 'His writing' is merely an explanatory conjunction to 'His destiny'. Why does he find this strange? He explains that destiny is an eternal attribute while writing is a temporal act.
The point is that taqdir (measuring) is eternal, but kitabah (writing) occurs after the Pen's creation.
4
Examine the proof from Imam Abu Hanifa
The author quotes a tradition from al-Wasiyya where God commands the Pen to write what will happen until the Day of Resurrection. This supports the descriptive nature of the writing.
The hadith is linked to Quran 54:52-53.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يكون في الدنيا ولا في الآخرة شيء أي موجود حادث في الأحوال جميعها (إلا) بمشيئته أي مقرونا بإرادته وعلمه وقضائه أي حكمه وأمره وقدره) أي بتقديره بقدر قدره (وكتبه) بفتح الكاف وسكون التاء أي وكتابته في اللوح المحفوظ) أي قبل ظهور أمره. وأغرب شارح حيث قال: وكتبه عطف تفسير لقدره. انتهى. وجه الغرابة أن ثبوت تقديره وتقريره مقدّم على تحريره وتصويره على أن التقدير صفة المنعوت بالقدم والكتابة حادثة بعد إحداث القلم. ولكن كتبه بالوصف لا بالحكم) أي كتب الله في حق كل شيء بأنه سيكون كذا وكذا لم يكتب بأنه ليكُن كذا وكذا، وتوضيحه أن وقت الكتابة لم تكن الأشياء موجودة، فكتب في اللوح المحفوظ على وجه الوصف أنه ستكون الأشياء على وفق القضاء لا على وجه الأمر بأنه ليكن؛ لأنه لو قال ليكن لكانت الأشياء كلها موجودةً حينئذ لعدم تصور تخلف المخلوق عن الأمر الإيجادي للخالق. وقال الإمام الأعظم في كتابه "الوصية": نقر بأن الله تعالى أمر القلم بأن يكتب، وفي نسخة بأن اكتب، فقال القلم : ماذا أكتب يارب؟ فقال الله تعالى : اكتب ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيمة. لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ فَعَلُوهُ فِي الزُّبُرِ وَكُلُّ صَغِيرٍ وَ كَبِيرٍ مُسْتَطَرْ﴾ [القمر: ٥٢-٥٣] ، انتهى . الحديث مقتبس من القرآن؛ لأنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم كان في معرض التبيان.
And nothing occurs in the world nor in the Hereafter (i.e., no originated existent in all circumstances) except by His will, i.e., accompanied by His will and knowledge and His decree, i.e., His judgment and command, and His destiny, i.e., His measuring with a proper measure, and His writing (with fatha on kaf and sukun on ta), i.e., His writing in the Preserved Tablet, i.e., before the appearance of His command. And a commentator made a strange claim where he said: 'And His writing' is an explanatory conjunction to 'His destiny'. End. The strangeness is that the establishment of His measuring and deciding is prior to its detailing and depicting, given that measuring is an attribute qualified by eternity, while writing occurs after the creation of the Pen. But His writing is by description, not by command. i.e., Allah wrote concerning each thing that it will be such and such; He did not write that it should be such and such. Its clarification is that at the time of writing, things did not exist, so He wrote in the Preserved Tablet in the manner of description that things will occur according to the decree, not in the manner of command that it should be; because if He had said 'let it be', everything would have existed at that time, since it is inconceivable that the creature would lag behind the creative command of the Creator. And the Great Imam said in his book 'al-Wasiyya': 'We affirm that Allah Almighty commanded the Pen to write, and in another copy: 'Write', so the Pen said: 'What shall I write, O Lord?' So Allah Almighty said: 'Write what will happen until the Day of Resurrection', according to His saying Exalted: 'And every thing they have done is in the scriptures, and every small and great is inscribed.' (al-Qamar: 52-53). End. The hadith is adapted from the Quran, because he (peace and blessings be upon him) was in the context of explanation.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a detailed doctrinal explanation (tafsir) of the phrase 'nothing occurs except by His will... and His writing'. The author gives a word-for-word gloss: 'His will' means accompanied by His will and knowledge, 'His decree' means His judgment and command, 'His destiny' means His measuring, and 'His writing' means His writing in the Preserved Tablet before the event occurs. He then criticizes a commentator who claimed that 'His writing' is merely an explanatory repetition of 'His destiny'. The author objects: measuring (taqdir) is an eternal attribute, while writing is a temporal act after the creation of the Pen. Then the author clarifies the nature of this writing: it is descriptive (bi al-wasf), not prescriptive (bi al-hukm). God writes that things will be such-and-such, not that they should be; if it were a command, everything would have existed instantaneously. To support this, the author cites a tradition from Imam Abu Hanifa's book al-Wasiyya, where God commands the Pen to write what will happen until the Day of Resurrection, with a Qur'anic proof (al-Qamar: 52-53). Finally, the author notes that the hadith is derived from the Qur'an because the Prophet was explaining it.

Key Terms
اللوح المحفوظ
كتبه
الوصف
الحكم
التقدير
القلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's writing in the Preserved Tablet is a command that forces events to instantly occur.
Correction: God's writing is a description of what will happen according to His eternal decree, not a creative command. If it were a command, everything would exist at that moment.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the view that 'His writing' is an explanatory conjunction to 'His destiny'?
A) Because writing is eternal like destiny.
B) Because writing is a created act after the Pen, while destiny is an eternal attribute.
C) Because writing and destiny are the same thing.
D) Because the Pen is uncreated.

Key Takeaway
God's writing in the Preserved Tablet is a description of what will happen, not a command that necessitates immediate existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a painful event from your past that you wish had not happened. Knowing that God's writing is descriptive, not a command that compelled that event, how does this change your view of God's role? Does it help you trust His wisdom even when you don't understand? Now, can you honestly thank Him for it? If not, what is holding you back, and will you ask Him for the strength to do so?
?
The distinction between descriptive and prescriptive is subtle. In your own life, do you ever treat God's will as a rigid command that leaves you no personal responsibility? For example, when you sin, do you blame it on 'destiny'? How does this lesson call you to take ownership of your choices while still trusting in God's overarching decree? What is one practical step you can take this week to live with this balance?
?
Imam Abu Hanifa reported that God told the Pen to write everything that will happen until the Day of Resurrection. Every deed—small or great—is inscribed. As you reflect on this, does it fill you with hope or fear? Perhaps both. What would it mean for you to live today as if every action is being recorded? How can this awareness lead you to more sincere repentance and a deeper reliance on God's mercy? Commit to one concrete change in your daily habit starting tomorrow.

The Attribute of Will (Mashi'ah) as Eternal Without Modality
Sanusi affirms that al-mashi'ah is an eternal attribute without modality and explains the two approaches of believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attribute of will (mashi'ah) is an eternal attribute of Allah, known only in its reality through revelation, and that reason cannot grasp its modality; you will also learn the two approaches of believers regarding such attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's will is real but unknowable in how – reason submits, faith affirms.

This lesson explores one of the profound teachings of Sunni theology: affirming Allah's attributes without attempting to understand how they are. Imam Sanusi clarifies that the attribute of will (mashi'ah) is eternal and established by revelation, yet its modality is unknown. He then distinguishes between two types of believers: those who investigate and those who refrain, showing that the latter's faith is stronger.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the main point about the attribute of will and the two groups of believers.
Notice the dense style and the quotation from Shams al-A'imma.
2
Identify the key terms
Note the terms 'al-mashi'ah', 'bila kayf', 'mutashabiha', and understand their significance in the context of divine attributes.
These terms are foundational in Sunni theology.
3
Understand the two categories of believers
Analyze the distinction between the believer who delves into seeking (due to ignorance) and the one who refrains (due to being honored with knowledge). Consider why the second approach is considered stronger.
The second approach reflects pure faith in the unseen.
4
Reflect on the role of reason
Consider why the author says reason is invalid in describing these attributes and how this relates to the concept of tafwid (consigning the true nature to Allah).
Reason has no scope in matters of divine essence and attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشيئة أي الإرادة المتعلقة بها صفاته في الأزل بلا كيف، أي بلا وصف لذلك العمل والمعنى أن هذه الثلاث المذكورة صفات في الأزل ثابتة بالكتاب والسنة، إلا أنها متشابهة الصفة مجهولة الكيفية كسائر صفاته العَلِيّة حيث حقيقتها خفيّة عن البريّة، فيجب على المؤمن بها أن يؤمن ويعتقد أن موجب العقل باطل في وصفها، إذ ليس من شأنه أن يدركها. وكذلك يقول كل راسخ في العلم عند حكمها. قال شمس الأئمة رحمه الله : وهذا لأن المؤمنين فريقان مبتلى بالإمعان في الطلب لضرب من الجهل به، ومبتلى بالوقوف عن الطلب لكونه مكرّماً بنوع من العلم فيه، ومعنى الابتلاء من هذا الوجه ربما يزيد على معنى الابتلاء في الوجه الأول، فإن الابتلاء بمجرد الاعتقاد مع التوقف في طلب المراد بيان أن العقل لا يوجب شيئا ولا يدفع شيئا، فإنه يلزمه اعتقاد الحقية فيما لا مجال للعقل فيه ليعرف أن الحكم لله يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد. انتهى. وحاصله: أن الوجه الثاني هو الأقوى، فإنه إيمان بالأمر الغيبي اللاريبي الذي لا حظ للعقل فيه ولا لذة للطبع بل مجرد اتباع الحقِّ على ما ورد به السمع من جانب الشرع، بخلاف الأول.
And al-mashi'ah, meaning the will (irada) related to it, is among His attributes in eternity without how (bila kayf), that is, without describing that action. The meaning is that these three mentioned attributes are attributes in eternity, established by the Book and the Sunnah, except that they are similar in description, unknown in modality, like His other high attributes, the reality of which is hidden from creatures. Therefore, the believer must believe in them and hold that the dictate of reason is invalid in describing them, for it is not its function to comprehend them. And every deeply-rooted in knowledge says the same regarding their judgment. Shams al-A'imma (may Allah have mercy on him) said: This is because the believers are two groups: one tested by delving into seeking, due to a kind of ignorance about Him, and the other tested by refraining from seeking, because he is honored with a kind of knowledge in it. The meaning of test from this aspect may surpass the meaning of test in the first aspect, for the test by mere belief with stopping from seeking the desired clarifies that reason neither necessitates anything nor repels anything. For he must believe in the truth of that which reason has no scope, in order to know that judgment belongs to Allah; He does as He wills and decrees as He desires. End. The sum is that the second aspect is stronger, for it is faith in an unseen matter, without doubt, which has no share for reason and no pleasure for nature, but merely following the truth according to what the revealed law (sam') has conveyed from the side of the Shari'a, unlike the first aspect.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of the attribute of al-mashi'ah (will) as an eternal attribute without modality (bila kayf). The author clarifies that 'will' here means the divine will (irada) associated with actions, and it is one of Allah's eternal attributes described in revelation but unknown in how. The phrase 'these three mentioned attributes' likely refers to attributes discussed earlier in the text (possibly life, knowledge, will, etc., but only will is mentioned here). The author stresses that these attributes are 'mutashabiha al-sifa' (similar in description) and 'majhula al-kayfiyya' (unknown in modality), like all of Allah's attributes: their true reality is hidden from creatures. Therefore, the believer must affirm them and recognize that reason ('aql) cannot grasp their true nature—indeed, reason is invalid in describing them. This is the position of all those firmly rooted in knowledge. Then he quotes Shams al-A'imma, who divides believers into two categories regarding these attributes: one group is tested by delving into investigation, due to ignorance; the other is tested by refraining from seeking, because of being honored with a kind of knowledge. The second group's test is perhaps greater, as they rest content with mere belief without attempting to reason about the nature of these attributes. This demonstrates that reason does not necessitate or repel anything in this domain; rather, one must simply affirm the truth of what revelation conveys. The author concludes that the second approach is stronger: it is pure faith in the unseen, with no role for reason or natural inclination, but simply following the truth as received from the Shari'a.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الإرادة
بلا كيف
متشابهة الصفة
مجهولة الكيفية
راسخ في العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming attributes without modality means denying their actual existence.
Correction: The passage affirms that the attributes are real and established by revelation, but their true nature (kayfiyya) is unknown. Denying existence would contradict the very purpose of affirming them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a believer do regarding the attribute of will (mashi'ah) and similar attributes?
A) Investigate their true nature using reason.
B) Deny them due to their incomprehensibility.
C) Believe in them and hold that reason cannot describe them.
D) Accept only those attributes mentioned in the Quran literally.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of will is real and eternal, but its modality is unknown; the strongest faith is to affirm it without intellectual investigation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah's will is eternal but beyond your comprehension, does your heart feel peace in submission or restlessness in not knowing? Will you today surrender your need to understand, and simply say 'I believe'?
?
Which of the two groups do you find yourself in when facing verses or hadith about Allah's attributes—do you try to rationalize them or do you refrain from seeking explanations? Are you willing to accept that your intellect is not the measure of truth?
?
Is there an attribute of Allah that you have tried to 'figure out' or explain away? Will you now choose to honor it by silence, trusting that what He revealed is true even if you cannot grasp its modality?

The Eternal Nature of Allah's Will
Sanusi asserts the eternity of God's will and refutes created will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's will is an eternal attribute that specifies existents, and that the Karramiyya and some Mu'tazila erred by claiming it is created.

Core Idea
Allah's will is eternal, not created, and governs all existence.

Imam Abu Hanifa repeatedly emphasizes the attribute of will to establish its eternity and refute those who diminish it. This lesson focuses on his assertion that the will is an eternal attribute that specifies all things, and his refutation of the Karramiyya and some Mu'tazila who claimed it is created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the eternal will
Read the Arabic passage once to understand the author's claim that God's will is eternal and specifies existents.
Notice that the Imam repeats mention of the will to assert its eternity.
2
Understand the refutation of created will
The passage refutes the Karramiyya and some Mu'tazila who claim God's will is created. Understand why their view contradicts the attribute's eternity.
3
Reflect on the necessity of an eternal will
Consider why God's will must be eternal—if it were created, it would imply change and contingency in God.
This is a key point in Ash'ari and Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد كرر الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله ذكر الإرادة هنا تحقيقا لكونها صفة قديمة لله تعالى تخصص المكوّنات بوجه دون وجه في وقت دون وقت وردا على الكرامية وبعض المعتزلة إرادته حادثة، وأما جمهورهم فأنكروا إرادته للشرور والقبائح، حتى يقولوا: إنه سبحانه وتعالى أراد من الكافر والفاسق إيمانه وطاعته لا كفره ،ومعصيته، زعما منهم أن إرادة القبيح قبيحة كخلقه وإيجاده، وهو ممنوع ومدفوع بأن القبيح هو كسبه والاتصاف به، فعندهم يكون أكثر ما يقع من أفعال الخلق على خلاف ما أراد الله في البلاد، وهذا شنيع جداً حيث لا يصبر على ذلك رئيس قرية من العباد.
And the Greatest Imam (may God have mercy on him) repeated the mention of the will here to affirm that it is an eternal attribute of God Almighty that specifies existents in one way rather than another at one time rather than another, as a refutation of the Karramiyya and some Mu'tazila who say that His will is created. As for the majority of them, they denied His will for evils and abominations, so that they say: He, exalted, willed from the disbeliever and the sinner faith and obedience, not disbelief and disobedience, claiming from them that the will of the ugly is ugly like its creation and bringing into existence. And this is prevented and refuted by the fact that the ugly is [the servant's] acquisition and being described by it. According to them, most of what occurs of the actions of creatures would be contrary to what God willed in the lands, and this is very repugnant, as not even a village chief would tolerate that.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two heretical positions regarding the divine will. The author states that Imam Abu Hanifa repeatedly mentions the will to confirm that it is an eternal attribute that specifies things in specific ways and times. This is a response to the Karramiyya and some Mu'tazila who claim that God's will is created. More importantly, the majority of the Mu'tazila deny that God wills evil and abominations; they claim that God only wills faith and obedience from the disbeliever and sinner, not their disbelief. Their argument is that willing evil is itself evil, like creating it. The author refutes this by pointing out that evil lies in the servant's acquisition (kash) and being described by it, not in God's act. Moreover, if God did not will evil, then most human actions would occur contrary to His will, which is absurd—no village chief would tolerate such a situation.

Key Terms
الإرادة (al-irādah)
الكرامية (al-Karramiyyah)
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazilah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's will is created like other creations.
Correction: The passage affirms that God's will is an eternal attribute, not created, because if it were created, it would need another will to create it, leading to infinite regress.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Imam Abu Hanifa repeat mention of the will?
A) To show that the will is a created attribute
B) To affirm that it is an eternal attribute and refute those who say it is created
C) To argue that God's will changes over time
D) To prove that will is not a real attribute

Key Takeaway
God's will is an eternal attribute that specifies all existents, refuting those who claim it is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's will is eternal and specifies every detail of your existence, why do you sometimes resent His decree in your life? What would it mean to surrender to a will that has always been there, even before you were born?
?
The Karramiyya and Mu'tazila claimed His will is created—meaning it could change or be influenced. Do you ever act as if God's will is created, by doubting that His plan for you is already perfect and unchangeable? How can you live today in submission to that eternal will?
?
The passage says God's will 'specifies existents in one way rather than another at one time rather than another.' When you look at your past disappointments, can you see them as part of that specification? What would it take for you to trust that His timing and manner are exactly what you need?

Refutation of the Denial of God's Will for Evil
Sanusi refutes the Mu'tazila denial of God's will for evil using rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila denial of God's will for evil is false, and that evil is attributed to human acquisition, not to God's will.

Core Idea
God wills both good and evil; human acquisition, not divine will, is the locus of moral evil.

The majority of the Mu'tazila claimed that God does not will evil, arguing that willing evil is itself evil. This lesson presents the refutation: evil lies in the servant's acquisition, and denying God's will for evil leads to the absurd consequence that most human actions contradict God's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila claim and their argument
Read the passage carefully to understand what the Mu'tazila claim about God's will for evil and their reasoning.
They claim God wills only good from disbelievers, not their disbelief.
2
Understand the refutation based on acquisition (kasb)
The author refutes by stating that evil is in the servant's acquisition and description, not in God's will. Grasp this distinction.
This is a key Ash'ari concept: actions are created by God but acquired by humans.
3
Grasp the absurd consequence of their position
If God does not will evil, then most human actions would be contrary to His will, which is absurd—even a village chief would not tolerate such disorder.
This shows that the Mu'tazila view implies a lack of divine sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage is a refutation of two heretical positions regarding the divine will. The author states that Imam Abu Hanifa repeatedly mentions the will to confirm that it is an eternal attribute that specifies things in specific ways and times. This is a response to the Karramiyya and some Mu'tazila who claim that God's will is created. More importantly, the majority of the Mu'tazila deny that God wills evil and abominations; they claim that God only wills faith and obedience from the disbeliever and sinner, not their disbelief. Their argument is that willing evil is itself evil, like creating it. The author refutes this by pointing out that evil lies in the servant's acquisition (kash) and being described by it, not in God's act. Key Terms
الإرادة (al-irādah)
الكسب (al-kasb)
القبيح (al-qabīh)
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazilah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Willing evil makes God unjust or evil.
Correction: Evil is attributed to human acquisition, not to God's will; God's will is the source of existence, not moral evil.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the absurd consequence of the Mu'tazila denial that God wills evil?
A) God would not be all-knowing
B) Most human actions would be contrary to God's will
C) Evil would not exist
D) Humans would have no free will

Key Takeaway
God's will encompasses all things, including evil, but evil is morally attributed to human acquisition, not to divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that God willed that sin to occur? If so, how does that affect your repentance and your view of God's justice? Be honest: are you tempted to blame God for your failures?
?
The passage argues that if God willed only good, then most human actions would oppose His will, which is absurd. How does this truth change the way you understand the presence of evil in your life? Will you now submit to God's will even in hardship, knowing He wills it for a purpose?
?
You claim to believe that God's will is all-encompassing. But do you live as if your choices can thwart His plan? What would change today if you fully embraced that every event in your life — even your sins — occurs by God's will and yet you are responsible for your acquisition? Write one concrete step to align your heart with this truth.

The Eternal Attribute of Divine Will and Refutation of Those Who Deny It
Affirmation of eternal divine will and refutation of Mu'tazila and Karamiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine will is an eternal attribute and how the author refutes the Mu'tazila and Karamiyya positions.

Core Idea
Divine will is eternal; ugliness lies in the act, not in the willing.

This passage from the Sharh of al-Fiqh al-Akbar continues the discussion of divine attributes, focusing on the attribute of will (al-irāda). The author affirms that Allah's will is eternal and not created, and he refutes two groups: the Karamiyya who claim it is temporal, and the Mu'tazila who deny that Allah wills evil. Understanding this argument clarifies a key point of Sunni theology regarding divine will and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly and then the English translation. Notice the structure: first the affirmation of eternal will, then the refutation of two positions.
The author uses a refutational style.
2
Identify the two groups being refuted
Find where the author mentions the Karamiyya and the Mu'tazila. What do each of them believe? What is the difference between their positions?
The Karamiyya and some Mu'tazila say will is temporal; the majority Mu'tazila deny willing evil.
3
Understand the argument about ugliness
The Mu'tazila claim that willing evil is ugly. The author refutes by saying ugliness is in the kasb (acquisition) and characterization. Think about what that means for divine will.
This is a key theological nuance.
4
Reflect on the reductio ad absurdum
The author points out that if the Mu'tazila were correct, most human actions would be against Allah's will, which is absurd. Consider the analogy of a village chief.
This shows the logical consequence of the Mu'tazilite position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد كرر الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله ذكر الإرادة هنا تحقيقا لكونها صفة قديمة لله تعالى تخصص المكوّنات بوجه دون وجه في وقت دون وقت وردا على الكرامية وبعض المعتزلة إرادته حادثة، وأما جمهورهم فأنكروا إرادته للشرور والقبائح، حتى يقولوا: إنه سبحانه وتعالى أراد من الكافر والفاسق إيمانه وطاعته لا كفره ومعصيته، زعما منهم أن إرادة القبيح قبيحة كخلقه وإيجاده، وهو ممنوع ومدفوع بأن القبيح هو كسبه والاتصاف به، فعندهم يكون أكثر ما يقع من أفعال الخلق على خلاف ما أراد الله في البلاد، وهذا شنيع جداً حيث لا يصبر على ذلك رئيس قرية من العباد.
The Great Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, repeated mention of will here to affirm that it is an eternal attribute of Allah, may He be exalted, that specifies created things in one way rather than another, at one time rather than another, in refutation of the Karamiyya and some Mu'tazila who say that His will is temporally originated. As for their majority, they denied His willing of evils and ugly things, to the extent that they say: He, exalted and transcendent, willed from the disbeliever and the sinner faith and obedience, not disbelief and disobedience, claiming that willing the ugly is ugly like creating and bringing it into existence. This is prohibited and refuted by the fact that the ugly is the acquisition (kasb) of it and the characterization by it. Thus, according to them, most of what occurs of the actions of creatures is contrary to what Allah willed in the lands, and this is very disgraceful, such that the chief of a village would not tolerate it from his servants.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the divine attribute of will (al-irāda). The author notes that Imam Abu Hanifa (the Great Imam) repeatedly mentioned will in his works to establish it as an eternal attribute of Allah. This attribute specifies created things (al-mukawwanāt) in specific ways at specific times. This refutes two groups: (1) the Karamiyya and some Mu'tazila who claim that Allah's will is created (haditha), and (2) the majority of Mu'tazila who deny that Allah wills evil and ugly acts (shurūr wa qabā'iḥ). The Mu'tazila claim that Allah only wills faith and obedience from the disbeliever and sinner, not their disbelief and disobedience, because they think that willing ugliness would be ugly itself, similar to creating it. The author refutes this by stating that the ugliness lies in the acquisition (kasb) of the act and the characterization by it, not in the divine will. Moreover, if the Mu'tazila were correct, then most of what happens in the world would be contrary to Allah's will, which is absurd — even a village chief would not tolerate such a situation from his subjects.

Key Terms
الإرادة
صفة قديمة
الكرامية
المعتزلة
القبيح
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Willing evil is itself evil, so Allah cannot will evil.
Correction: The author argues that ugliness lies in the human acquisition and characterization of the act, not in the divine will. Allah's will is not morally evaluated like human acts.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that Allah does not will evil?
A) Allah is too exalted to will evil
B) Evil lies in the acquisition and characterization, not in the will
C) The Quran proves Allah wills evil
D) The Mu'tazila are heretics

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is eternal and encompasses all things, including evil; the evil lies in human acquisition, not divine decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah wills everything that happens, including your sins, do you use that as an excuse to avoid repentance? The lesson says the ugliness of sin lies in your acquisition. Which sin have you been blaming on Allah's will instead of taking full responsibility? Will you repent and resolve to change today?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed Allah only wills good from you—do you secretly believe that when you sin, it somehow escapes Allah's will? When you face a trial, do you trust that it is from His will and wisdom, or do you complain? What is one trial you can accept as His decree and respond with patience and gratitude?
?
Imagine a leader who cannot tolerate disobedience from his servants, yet Allah tolerates your daily failures and still provides for you. How does this reality strike your heart? What specific act of obedience will you offer today as a response to His immense patience and mercy?

The Particularization of God's Power
Explains the particularization of God's power by His will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's power is limited to what He wills, and why it is not said He is powerful over the impossible.

Core Idea
God's power only applies to what He wills.

This lesson explores a key distinction in Islamic theology: the general Quranic statement that Allah is powerful over all things is particularized by His will. We'll see why impossible things are excluded from His power and how to speak reverently about this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the principle 'every general statement is particularized'.
2
Identify the particularization
Find the general statement (Quran 2:284) and how it is particularized by what Allah wills. What is excluded?
Excluded are His essence, attributes, unwilled creatures, and impossible things.
3
Understand the conclusion about power
The passage concludes that power is attached only where will is attached. Reflect on why one does not say 'He is powerful over the impossible' nor 'He is not powerful'.
This shows reverence and logical consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وقد قيل: كل عام يخص، كما خص قوله تعالى: {والله على كل شيء قدير} [البقرة: 284] بما شاءه، ليخرج ذاته وصفاته، وما لم يشأ من مخلوقاته، وما يكون من المحال وقوعه في كائناته. والحاصل أن كل شيء تعلقت به مشيئته تعلقت به قدرته، وإلا فلا يقال "هو قادر على المحال"؛ لعدم وقوعه ولزوم كذبه، ولا يقال غير قادر عليه تعظيما لأدبه من ربه. ثم هذا العام مخصوص بقوله تعالى: {والله بكل شيء عليم} [التغابن: 11] فإنه باق على العموم وشامل للموجود والمعدوم والمحال والموهوم، كما بينه الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله بقوله: (يعلم الله تعالى المعدوم في حال عدمه معدوما) أي بوصف المعدومية، ويعلم أنه كيف يكون إذا أوجده) أي في عالم الربوبية، بل ويعلم أن شيئا لا يكون ولو كان كيف يكون.
It has been said: Every general statement is particularized, just as His saying—exalted: {And Allah is over all things powerful} [al-Baqarah: 284] is particularized by what He wills, to exclude His essence and attributes, and what He has not willed of His creatures, and what is impossible to occur among contingent things. The conclusion is that every thing to which His will is attached, His power is attached to it; otherwise one does not say 'He is powerful over the impossible' because of its non-occurrence and necessary falsehood, nor is it said 'He is not powerful over it' out of reverence for the servant's Lord. Then this general statement is specified by His saying—exalted: {And Allah is of all things knowing} [at-Taghabun: 11] for it remains general and includes the existent, the non-existent, the impossible, and the imaginary, as the Greatest Imam—may Allah have mercy on him—explained with his saying: 'Allah—exalted—knows the non-existent while it is non-existent' that is, with the description of non-existence, 'and He knows how it would be if He were to bring it into existence' that is, in the world of lordship, rather, He knows that a thing will not be, and if it were to be, how it would be.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a theological discussion on the generalization and particularization of two divine attributes: power and knowledge. The author begins with the principle that general statements are often particularized. As an example, the general statement 'Allah is powerful over all things' (Quran 2:284) is particularized by what He wills: it excludes His own essence and attributes (over which His power does not operate), things He does not will to create, and impossible things. The conclusion is that only things to which His will is attached have His power attached. One does not say He is powerful over the impossible because it never occurs and saying so would be false, nor does one say He is not powerful over it out of reverence. Then the author notes that the general statement 'Allah is knowing of all things' (Quran 64:11) remains general and is not particularized; it includes the existent, the non-existent, the impossible, and the imaginary. This is confirmed by the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa: Allah knows the non-existent as non-existent, and knows how it would be if created. The passage thus distinguishes between God's power (limited to what He wills) and His knowledge (unlimited, covering all possibilities).

Key Terms
عام
خاص
مشيئة
قدرة
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's power is absolutely unlimited, including over impossibilities.
Correction: This passage shows God's power is limited to what He wills; impossibilities are excluded, as saying He is powerful over them would be false.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it not said that Allah is powerful over the impossible?
A) Because it would imply a limitation in His power
B) Because the impossible never occurs and saying so would be false
C) Because the Quran does not mention it
D) Because the impossible is not a thing

Key Takeaway
God's power is confined to what He wills, and one must not attribute to Him power over the impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Allah is over all things powerful', do you ever pause to consider that His power is not attached to everything you desire—only to what He wills? How does that reshape the way you ask Him for things?
?
Is there something in your life that you believe is impossible for Allah to do because it seems contradictory to His will? How does this lesson challenge you to remain silent in reverence rather than assert what He can or cannot do?
?
If you truly internalized that Allah's power follows His wisdom and will—not your assumptions—what would change about the way you trust Him with your most difficult circumstances starting today?

God's All-Encompassing Knowledge
Affirms the generality of God's knowledge and explains His knowledge of the non-existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's knowledge is unlimited, encompassing even the non-existent and impossible, as explained by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
God's knowledge covers everything, even the impossible.

In contrast to power, God's knowledge remains general and unrestricted. This lesson examines how the Quranic statement 'Allah is knowing of all things' includes even the non-existent and the impossible, as clarified by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast with power.
The passage begins with 'ثم' indicating a shift.
2
Identify the scope of knowledge
Find the Quranic verse mentioned and see what it includes: existent, non-existent, impossible, imaginary.
Imam Abu Hanifa's explanation elaborates on this.
3
Break down Imam Abu Hanifa's statement
The Imam gives three points about God's knowledge of the non-existent. List them and understand each.
They cover knowledge of the non-existent as non-existent, knowledge of how it would be if created, and knowledge of what will never be.

Source Text

This passage is a theological discussion on the generalization and particularization of two divine attributes: power and knowledge. The author begins with the principle that general statements are often particularized. As an example, the general statement 'Allah is powerful over all things' (Quran 2:284) is particularized by what He wills: it excludes His own essence and attributes (over which His power does not operate), things He does not will to create, and impossible things. Misconception & Correction

Correction: This passage shows God's knowledge extends to non-existent things, impossibilities, and imaginary concepts.

Checkpoint

A) Only that it does not exist

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's knowledge includes every impossible scenario and every alternate reality that never came to be, how does this challenge your attachment to the 'what ifs' of your life? Are you able to surrender the regrets and hypothetical better outcomes to the One who knows that even if they were possible, He chose what is best for you? Commit to letting go of one specific 'what if' this week, trusting that Allah's knowledge is perfect and His decree is best.
?
Consider a sin you might be tempted to commit in private. Allah knows that sin even before you do it, and knows exactly how it would affect your soul and your life if you were to commit it. Does this knowledge change your intention when no one is watching? Resolve to remember that Allah's knowledge of the non-existent makes Him present with you even in your thoughts.
?
The passage says Allah knows that a thing will not be, and if it were to be, how it would be. Are you anxious about future outcomes that Allah knows will never happen? How can you turn that anxiety into trust in His all-encompassing knowledge? Practice saying 'Allah knows best' whenever your mind wanders to fears about what might be, and act on what He has commanded you to do today.

The Generality and Specificity of Allah's Power and Knowledge
Commentator distinguishes the scope of divine power and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's power is specified by His will while His knowledge remains unrestricted.

Core Idea
Allah's power is limited to what He wills, but His knowledge knows all.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a critical distinction between two of Allah's attributes: qudrah (power) and ʿilm (knowledge). While both are described as 'over all things' in the Quran, they are not equal in scope. This lesson will explore why Allah's power is specified by His will, whereas His knowledge embraces even the impossible and imaginary.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get the gist of the argument.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Notice that the commentator cites two verses: one about power (Al-Baqarah 2:109?) and one about knowledge (At-Talaq 65:12?). Observe how each is treated differently.
The power verse is specified; the knowledge verse remains general.
3
Understand the specification of power
The commentator argues that 'Allah is over all things Powerful' is specified by His will, excluding His essence, attributes, and impossible things. Ask yourself: what does this imply about Allah's power?
4
Contrast with the universality of knowledge
The verse about knowledge is left general, including even the impossible and imaginary. Note the example from Imam Abu Hanifa explaining how Allah knows non-existent things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وقد قيل: كل عام يخص كما خص قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ بما شاءه ليخرج ذاته وصفاته، وما لم يشأ من مخلوقاته، وما يكون من المحال وقوعه في كائناته. والحاصل أن كل شيء تعلقت به مشيئته تعلقت به قدرته وإلا فلا يقال "هو قادر على المحال"؛ لعدم وقوعه ولزوم كذبه ولا يقال غير قادر عليه تعظيماً لأدبه من ربه، ثم هذا العام مخصوص بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ﴾ فإنه باق على العموم وشامل للموجود والمعدوم والمحال والموهوم كما بينه الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله بقوله: (يعلم الله تعالى المعدوم في حال عدمه معدوماً) أي بوصف المعدومية، ويعلم أنه كيف يكون إذا أوجده) أي في عالم الربوبية، بل ويعلم أن شيئاً لا يكون ولو كان كيف يكون.
This has been said: Every general term is specified just as He specified His saying: 'And Allah is over all things Powerful' by what He willed, to exclude His Essence and His Attributes, and what He did not will of His creatures, and what is impossible to occur among existing things. The conclusion is that everything to which His will is attached, His power is attached to it; otherwise it is not said 'He is powerful over the impossible' because of its non-occurrence and the necessary falsity, nor is it said 'He is not powerful over it' out of reverence for the conduct of His servant. Then this general term is specified by His saying: 'And Allah is of all things Knowing', for it remains general and inclusive of the existent, the non-existent, the impossible, and the imaginary, as explained by the Great Imam (may Allah have mercy on him) in his saying: (Allah knows the non-existent in the state of its non-existence as non-existent) i.e., with the attribute of non-existence, and He knows how it would be if He brought it into existence, i.e., in the realm of lordship. Rather, He knows that a thing will not be, and if it were, how it would be.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a theological clarification about the scope of Allah's attributes of power (qudrah) and knowledge (ʿilm). The commentator begins by stating a general rule: every universal statement (ʿāmm) can be specified. He applies this to the verse 'And Allah is over all things Powerful'. This statement is not absolutely general; it is specified by Allah's will. Thus, Allah's power applies only to what He wills, excluding His own Essence and Attributes, what He does not will among creatures, and impossible things. Therefore, one should not say 'Allah is powerful over the impossible' because that would be false, nor should one say 'He is not powerful over it' out of reverence. In contrast, the verse 'And Allah is of all things Knowing' remains fully general, covering the existent, the non-existent, the impossible, and the imaginary. The commentator supports this with the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa (al-Imām al-Aʿẓam): 'Allah knows the non-existent in the state of its non-existence as non-existent, and He knows how it would be if He brought it into existence, and He knows that a thing will not be, and if it were, how it would be.' This demonstrates the all-encompassing nature of divine knowledge.

Key Terms
عام
خاص
قدرة
علم
محال
موهوم
مشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's power is absolutely unrestricted, even to logically impossible things.
Correction: Allah's power is only over what He wills; the impossible (e.g., creating a square circle) is not an object of power.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the scope of the verse 'And Allah is over all things Powerful'?
A) It is absolutely general, covering even the impossible.
B) It is specified by Allah's will, applying only to what He wills.
C) It applies only to existent things.
D) It applies only to non-existent things.

Key Takeaway
Allah's power is restricted to what He wills, but His knowledge encompasses everything, including the impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is powerful over all things,' do you include logical impossibilities in your mind? How will you correct your understanding after this lesson?
?
Allah knows even what will never happen and how it would be if it did. Does this thought humble you, knowing that nothing in your imagination or future is hidden from Him? How will you live differently today because of this?
?
This lesson shows that Allah's power is subject to His will. Are there times when you wish Allah had willed something differently for you? How does trusting His will—even when it contradicts your desires—reflect true servitude?

Allah's Knowledge: Eternal, Unchanging, and All-Encompassing
Commentator explains the immutability of Allah's knowledge using an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's knowledge of creation does not change, even when created things change states.

Core Idea
Allah's eternal knowledge encompasses all changes without itself changing.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a subtle point about divine knowledge: when a person stands and then sits, Allah knows him in both states, but His knowledge does not change. The example illustrates how Allah's pre-eternal knowledge includes every future state, so when that state occurs, no new knowledge arises. This teaching safeguards the immutability of Allah's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the full argument. Notice the example of standing and sitting.
Pay attention to the distinction between two types of knowledge mentioned.
2
Identify the two types of knowledge
The commentator distinguishes between 'definitive apparent knowledge' (علماً تنجيزياً ظاهرياً) and 'mental hidden knowledge' (ذهنياً وباطنياً). Understand how these relate to Allah's eternal knowledge.
The apparent knowledge occurs when the event happens, while the hidden knowledge was always present in eternity.
3
Reflect on the core principle
Consider why change in creatures does not imply change in Allah. The passage states that change and transition occur in creatures, while Allah is free from such attributes.
This principle is central to Sunni creed.
4
Review the variant reading
The commentator notes an addition 'or His attribute' in some copies. Understand that this does not affect the meaning but shows manuscript variations.
The core point remains that Allah's knowledge is eternal and unchanging.
5
Summarize the conclusion
The passage concludes: Allah's knowledge does not change, nor does His judgment differ, nor does new knowledge occur due to changes in existents.
Memorize this as a key creedal statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعلم الله تعالى الموجود في حال وجوده موجوداً) أي بعد أن علمه في حال عدمه معدوماً، ويعلم أنه كيف يكون فَناؤه أي إذا أراد أن يجعله معدوماً بعد أن علمه في حال وجوده موجوداً من غير تغير علمه تعالى في مراتب كونه معلوماً قائماً. ويعلم الله تعالى القائم في حال قيامه قائماً) أي مثلاً، وإلا فكذا في حال حياته وصلاته وصيامه وسائر مقاماته (وإذا قعد أي تغير عن حاله الأول علمه قاعداً في حال قعوده أي انتقاله حالة إلى حالة علماً تنجيزياً ظاهرياً بعد ما كان يعلم أنه سيقعد، إلا أن ذلك العلم كان ذهنياً وباطنياً كما حقق في تفسير قوله: ﴿ إِلَّا لِنَعْلَمَ مَنْ يَتَّبِعُ الرَّسُوْلَ مِمَّنْ يَنْقَلِبُ عَلى عَقِبَيْهِ ﴾ [البقرة: 143]، (من غير أن يتغير علمه) وزيد في نسخة: «أو صفته»، والظاهر أن الثاني وجد في نسخة بدل علمه، فألحقه به وما أبدله فحصل بسبب الجمع بعض خلل أو يحدث له علم أي في ثاني حاله ما لم يكن في أزله، ولكن التغير أي الانتقال واختلاف الأحوال أي من القيام والقعود وأمثالهما من الأفعال يحدث في المخلوقين مع تنزه الملك المتعال عن قبول الانفعال وحصول التغير والانتقال، فإن علمه قديم بالأشياء، فإذا أوجد شيئاً أو أفناه فإنما يوجده أو يفنيه على وفق ما علمه وطبق ما قدره وقضاه، فإذن لا يتغير علمه ولا يختلف حكمه ولا يحدث له علم بتغير الموجود والمعدوم، واختلافه وحدوثه.
And Allah knows the existent in the state of its existence as existent, i.e., after He knew it in the state of its non-existence as non-existent, and He knows how its annihilation will be, i.e., if He wills to make it non-existent after He knew it in the state of its existence as existent, without any change in His knowledge (exalted be He) in the stages of its being known as existing. And Allah knows the one standing in the state of his standing as standing, i.e., for example, and otherwise similarly in the state of his life, prayer, fasting, and all his states. And if he sits, i.e., changes from his first state, He knows him sitting in the state of his sitting, i.e., his transition from one state to another, with a definitive and apparent knowledge after He knew that he would sit, except that that knowledge was mental and hidden, as verified in the interpretation of His saying: 'Except that We may know who follows the Messenger from him who turns on his heels' [Al-Baqarah: 143]. (Without any change in His knowledge) and in some copies: 'or His attribute' is added. It appears that the second is found in a copy instead of 'His knowledge', so he attached it to it and did not replace it, so due to the combination some disorder occurred. Or that knowledge occurs to Him in the second state that was not in His pre-eternity. Rather, change, i.e., transition, and variation of states, i.e., from standing, sitting, and the like of actions, occur in creatures, while the Exalted King is free from receiving affection and undergoing change and transition. For His knowledge is eternal of things. So if He brings something into existence or annihilates it, He only brings it into existence or annihilates it in accordance with what He knew and in accordance with what He determined and decreed. Thus, His knowledge does not change, nor does His judgment differ, nor does knowledge occur to Him due to the change of the existent and non-existent and their variation and occurrence.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the creedal statement about Allah's knowledge of the existent. The commentator explains that just as Allah knows the non-existent as non-existent, He also knows the existent as existent, and He knows how it will cease to exist. This knowledge remains unchanged even when the thing changes states. For instance, Allah knows a person standing as standing, and when that person sits, He knows him sitting—not because His knowledge changes, but because He had already known eternally that the person would sit. The actual knowledge that appears at the moment of sitting is a 'definitive and apparent' (tanzījī ẓāhirī) knowledge, whereas the prior eternal knowledge was 'mental and hidden' (dhihnī bāṭinī). This distinction is supported by the verse 'except that We may know who follows the Messenger...'. The commentator notes a variant reading in some copies that adds 'or His attribute', but suggests that this may have caused some confusion. The core point is that change and variation are characteristics of creatures, not of Allah. Allah's knowledge is eternal (qadīm) and does not undergo alteration. When He creates or annihilates, it is in perfect accordance with His eternal knowledge and decree. Therefore, His knowledge does not change, nor does His judgment differ, and no new knowledge occurs due to changes in existing things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah acquires new knowledge when events occur, implying change in His attributes.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah's knowledge is eternal and encompasses all future states; when events happen, no new knowledge arises—the knowledge was already present, though hidden.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Allah's knowledge not change when a person sits after standing?
A) Because Allah's knowledge is created anew each moment.
B) Because He already knew eternally that the person would sit.
C) Because sitting does not affect knowledge.
D) Because Allah is not aware of changes.

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is eternal, unchanging, and encompasses all states of creation; changes in creation do not imply change in His knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an unexpected difficulty, do you truly believe that Allah knew it from eternity and permitted it for a reason? How does that change your first reaction of panic or complaint?
?
Allah's knowledge of you is complete and unchanging—He knows every thought and action before you do. Does this fill you with awe and accountability, or do you live as if some areas of your life are hidden from Him?
?
The source passage distinguishes between Allah's hidden knowledge and apparent knowledge. Are there challenges in your life where you need to trust His hidden knowledge—that He already knew you would face this and decreed it for your good?

God's Knowledge Does Not Change with Creatures' States
Commentary explains that God's knowledge is eternal and unchanged by creatures' states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's knowledge remains unchanged despite the changing states of creatures, and how this aligns with His eternal, all-embracing knowledge.

Core Idea
God's knowledge of all states is eternal; creatures change, but His knowledge does not.

This passage from the commentary on Fiqh al-Akbar tackles a potential misunderstanding: if God knows a person as standing, does He then 'learn' that they are sitting when they sit? The commentator clarifies that God's knowledge is eternal and encompasses all states from the beginning, so no new knowledge occurs. The change is only in the creature, not in God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repetition of examples (existent/non-existent, standing/sitting).
2
Identify the examples
The commentator uses two examples: God knows the existent as existent and its annihilation, and God knows the standing as standing and the sitting as sitting. See how these illustrate the principle.
3
Understand the distinction
Grasp the difference between God's eternal knowledge and the temporal realization of that knowledge in creation. The commentator uses the Quranic verse (2:143) to explain that some knowledge is 'mental and inner' before becoming 'effectively apparent'.
This is a key point: God's knowledge does not change; rather, the outward manifestation changes.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that change occurs only in creatures, while God is transcendent. His knowledge is eternal and His actions follow His prior knowledge and decree.
This reinforces the Sunni doctrine of eternal divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعلم الله تعالى الموجود في حال وجوده موجوداً، ويعلم أنه كيف يكون فَناؤه، ويعلم الله تعالى القائم في حال قيامه قائماً، وإذا قعد علمه قاعداً في حال قعوده من غير أن يتغير علمه أو يحدث له علم، ولكن التغير واختلاف الأحوال يحدث في المخلوقين. (ويعلم الله تعالى الموجود في حال وجوده موجوداً) أي بعد أن علمه في حال عدمه معدوما، ويعلم أنه كيف يكون فَناؤه أي إذا أراد أن يجعله معدوما بعد أن علمه في حال وجوده موجودا من غير تغير علمه تعالى في مراتب كونه معلوما قائما. ويعلم الله تعالى القائم في حال قيامه قائماً) أي مثلا، وإلا فكذا في حال حياته وصلاته وصيامه وسائر مقاماته (وإذا قعد أي تغير عن حاله الأول علمه قاعداً في حال قعوده أي انتقاله حالة إلى حالة علما من تنجيزيا ظاهريا بعد ما كان يعلم أنه سيقعد، إلا أن ذلك العلم كان ذهنيا وباطنيا كما حقق في تفسير قوله: ﴿ إِلَّا لِنَعْلَمَ مَنْ يَتَّبِعُ الرَّسُوْلَ مِمَّنْ يَنْقَلِبُ عَلى عَقِبَيْهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٤٣]، (من غير أن يتغير علمه) وزيد في نسخة: «أو صفته»، والظاهر أن الثاني وجد في نسخة بدل ،علمه، فألحقه به وما أبدله فحصل بسبب الجمع بعض خلل أو يحدث له علم أي في ثاني حاله ما لم يكن في أزله، ولكن التغير أي الانتقال واختلاف (الأحوال أي من القيام والقعود وأمثالهما من الأفعال (يحدث في المخلوقين مع تنزه الملك المتعال عن قبول الانفعال وحصول التغير والانتقال، فإن علمه قديم بالأشياء، فإذا أوجد شيئا أو أفناه فإنما يوجده أو يفنيه على وفق ما علمه وطبق ما قدره وقضاه، فإذن لا يتغير علمه ولا يختلف حكمه ولا يحدث له علم بتغير الموجود والمعدوم، واختلافه وحدوثه
And God Most High knows the existent, in the state of its existence, as existent, and He knows how its annihilation will be, and God Most High knows the one standing, in the state of his standing, as standing, and when he sits, He knows him as sitting, in the state of his sitting, without His knowledge changing or a knowledge occurring to Him, but change and difference of states occur in creatures. (And God Most High knows the existent, in the state of its existence, as existent) i.e., after He knew it, in the state of its non-existence, as non-existent, and He knows how its annihilation will be, i.e., when He wills to make it non-existent after He knew it, in the state of its existence, as existent, without any change in His knowledge, Most High, in the stages of its being known as existing. (And God Most High knows the one standing, in the state of his standing, as standing) i.e., for example, otherwise similarly in the state of his life, his prayer, his fasting, and all his stations. (And when he sits, i.e., changes from his first state, He knows him as sitting, in the state of his sitting, i.e., his transition from state to state, a knowledge that is effectively apparent after He knew that he would sit, except that that knowledge was mental and inner, as verified in the interpretation of His statement: 'Only that We may know who follows the Messenger from him who turns on his heels' [Quran 2:143]. (Without His knowledge changing) and in a copy it is added: 'or His attribute', and it appears that the second was found in a copy instead of 'His knowledge', so he appended it to it and did not replace it, and thus due to the combination some defect occurred. (Or a knowledge occurring to Him) i.e., in a second state that was not in His eternity. (But change, i.e., transition, and difference of states, i.e., of standing and sitting and the like of actions, occurs in creatures, while the Most High King is transcending the reception of passivity and the occurrence of change and transition. For His knowledge is eternal of things. So when He brings a thing into existence or annihilates it, He only brings it into existence or annihilates it in accordance with what He knew and in conformity with what He determined and decreed. Therefore, His knowledge does not change, nor does His judgment differ, nor does a knowledge of the change of the existent and non-existent and its difference and occurrence occur to Him.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a statement from the matn (Fiqh al-Akbar) regarding God's knowledge and its relation to changing states of creatures. The commentary first establishes that God knows the existent as existent and knows its future annihilation, and knows the standing person as standing and the sitting person as sitting—all without any change in His knowledge. The commentator emphasizes that God's knowledge is not affected by the transitions of creatures. He clarifies that when God knows a person's future sitting, that knowledge was initially 'mental and inner' (ذهنيا وباطنيا) and then becomes 'effectively apparent' (تنجيزيا ظاهريا) when the sitting actually occurs. This is likened to the verse 'until We know' (Quran 2:143), which is interpreted as a manifestation of knowledge. The commentator then addresses a variant textual issue: some copies add 'or His attribute' after 'His knowledge', suggesting it was substituted rather than added. He then reiterates that change and difference occur in creation, while God is transcendent above passivity and change. The conclusion is that God's knowledge is eternal, and when He creates or annihilates, it is according to His prior knowledge and decree; thus no change occurs in His knowledge or judgment.

Correction: God's knowledge is eternal and encompasses all states from the beginning. The change is only in the creature, not in God's knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why does God's knowledge not change when a person moves from standing to sitting?
A) Because God's knowledge is acquired gradually.
B) Because God knew the person's states from eternity and the change only appears in the creature.
C) Because God does not care about such changes.
D) Because the person's actions are illusions.

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is eternal and does not change; only creatures undergo change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Have you ever assumed your good deeds surprised God or added to His knowledge? How does realizing His knowledge is unchanging reshape your motivation for doing them?
?
What would it mean for your daily life if you truly lived with the awareness that every state—your standing, sitting, and even your hidden thoughts—was known to God from eternity? What specific change in your actions would that produce today?

The First Interpretation of the Covenant Verse
The first interpretation of the covenant verse with the prophetic hadith about predestination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first interpretation of the covenant verse, which emphasizes divine decree based on the hadith of Adam's offspring.

Core Idea
Divine decree precedes human action; Allah creates for Paradise or Hell and then guides the deeds accordingly.

This lesson presents the first of two interpretations of the covenant verse (āyat al-mīthāq) according to Al-Qunawi. It is based on a well-known hadith narrated by ʿUmar that illustrates how Allah's decree determines the destiny of every soul. The passage emphasizes that Allah's knowledge and will encompass all human actions, yet it also preserves human responsibility by linking deeds to the ultimate outcome.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic hadith and its translation to understand the narrative of Adam's offspring.
Notice the use of right hand for Paradise and left hand for Hell.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the two groups extracted from Adam: those for Paradise and those for Hell.
Allah declares their destiny before they act.
3
Examine the question about deeds
Consider the man's question: 'What is the point of deeds?' This challenges the idea of human effort.
4
Understand the Prophet's response
The Prophet explains that Allah employs the servant with deeds consistent with their predetermined destiny.
This harmonizes decree and action.
5
Connect to Aqeedah
Reflect on how this interpretation is held by the majority of Ahl al-Sunna and its implications for predestination.
Avoid fatalism; deeds are real and consequential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال القونوي رحمه الله : في تفسير الآية الكريمة قولان: أحدهما قول أهل التفسير وعليه جمع من أكابر الأئمة وأكثر أهل السنة والجماعة وهو ما روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه سئل عن هذه الآية، فقال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : ((إن الله تعالى خلق آدم ثم مسح ظهره بيمينه فاستخرج منه ذرية، فقال: خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ويعملون عمل أهل الجنة، ثم مسح ظهره بشماله فاستخرج منه ذرية ، فقال : خلقت هؤلاء للنار ويعملون عمل أهل النار، فقال رجل: يارسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقيم العمل ؟ فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: إن الله تعالى إذا خلق العبد للجنة استعمله بعمل أهل الجنة حتى يموت على عمل من أعمال أهل الجنة فيدخله به الجنة، وكذلك إذا خلق الله العبد للنار استعمله بعمل أهل النار حتى يموت على عمل من أعمال أهل النار فيدخله به النار))
Al-Qunawi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Concerning the interpretation of the noble verse, there are two sayings: One of them is the saying of the people of tafsir, and upon it is a group of the major imams and most of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, and it is what was narrated that 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, was asked about this verse and he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, say: 'Verily Allah the Exalted created Adam, then wiped his back with His right hand and brought forth offspring from him, and said: I created these for Paradise and they will do the deeds of the people of Paradise. Then He wiped his back with His left hand and brought forth offspring from him, and said: I created these for Hell and they will do the deeds of the people of Hell. A man said: O Messenger of Allah, then what is the point of deeds? The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: Verily Allah the Exalted, when He creates a servant for Paradise, He employs him with the deeds of the people of Paradise until he dies upon a deed from the deeds of the people of Paradise, and thus He enters him into Paradise. And likewise, when Allah creates a servant for Hell, He employs him with the deeds of the people of Hell until he dies upon a deed from the deeds of the people of Hell, and thus He enters him into Hell.'
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents the first of two interpretations of the covenant verse (āyat al-mīthāq) according to al-Qūnawī. It is the interpretation of the people of tafsīr, held by many major imams and the majority of Ahl al-Sunna. It is based on a narration from ʿUmar that the Prophet ﷺ said that Allah created Adam, then wiped his back with His right hand and extracted offspring, saying He created these for Paradise and they will do deeds of the people of Paradise. Then He wiped with His left hand and extracted offspring, saying He created these for Hell and they will do deeds of the people of Hell. A man asked about the point of deeds, and the Prophet replied that when Allah creates a person for Paradise, He makes him do deeds of Paradise until he dies on those deeds and enters Paradise, and similarly for Hell. This hadith emphasizes divine decree and predestination.

Key Terms
آية الميثاق
قول أهل التفسير
ذرية آدم
قضاء العمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This hadith is sometimes misinterpreted as supporting pure compulsion, negating human responsibility.
Correction: It actually emphasizes divine knowledge and decree without negating human responsibility; deeds are real and consistent with the decree.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this passage, what determines whether a person will enter Paradise or Hell?
A) Their own choice and deeds.
B) Allah's decree based on His knowledge.
C) The intercession of the Prophet.
D) Their lineage from Adam.

Key Takeaway
The first interpretation of the covenant verse affirms that Allah's decree determines the ultimate destiny of each person, and He guides them to deeds consistent with that decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah has already decreed your ultimate destination, what does this lesson demand of you regarding the sincerity and quality of your daily deeds? Is there any action you are currently doing that contradicts the destiny you hope for?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment, and He shows you that your deeds perfectly matched His decree for you. Does that thought fill you with hope or fear? What one change can you make today to align your deeds more closely with the deeds of the people of Paradise?
?
The man in the hadith asked, 'What is the point of deeds?' Have you ever felt that your efforts are futile? How does the Prophet's answer transform the way you will approach your next act of worship or obedience? Commit to one specific deed this week that you will perform with the awareness that Allah is employing you for a purpose.

Proof that Allah Creates All Human Actions
A set of proofs that Allah creates all human actions, concluding with a refutation of the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple proofs from the Quran, hadith, and reason that establish Allah as the Creator of all human actions.

Core Idea
Allah creates every human action, proven by scripture and reason.

The author compiles a comprehensive array of evidence to establish a core Sunni belief: that Allah is the Creator of all human actions. These proofs include clear Quranic verses, a prophetic hadith, a rational argument, and even a saying of Imam Ali. This passage also exposes a critical error of the Mu'tazila who misinterpreted a key verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall flow of proofs. Notice how the author moves from Quranic evidence to hadith to rational argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Examine the first Quranic proof (Az-Zumar 62)
Identify how the verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' is used. The author clarifies that 'everything' includes every possible thing, and the servant's action is a thing, so Allah creates it.
This verse is the foundation.
3
Examine the second and third proofs (An-Nahl 17, As-Saffat 96)
The verse from An-Nahl is presented in the context of worship: only the true Creator deserves worship. The verse from As-Saffat is used by Abu Hanifa against a Mu'tazila leader. Note the different angles.
Each verse targets a different aspect.
4
Consider the hadith and rational argument
Read the hadith 'Allah is the maker of every maker' and the rational argument that if a servant created his own actions, he would know their details. Reflect on how reason supports revelation.
The hadith is narrated by al-Hakim and al-Bayhaqi.
5
Understand the Mu'tazila error
The author criticizes the Mu'tazila for misinterpreting 'Allah is the Creator of everything' to refer only to attributes, not actions. This is a key sectarian point.
This shows the practical impact of the doctrine.

(والله تعالى خالقها أي موجد أفعال العباد وفق ما أراد لقوله تعالى: ﴿ اللَّهُ خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ الزمر : ٦٢] ، أي ممكن بدلالة العقل، وفعل العبد شيء ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَنْ يَخْلُقُ كَمَنْ لا يَخْلُقُ [النحل: ۱۷]، أي الذي يصدر منه حقيقة الخلق ليس كمن لا يصدر منه ذلك في شيء، وهذا في مقام التمدح بالخالقية وكونها سببا لاستحقاق العبادة. ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ [الصافات: ٩٦ ] ، أي وعملكم أو معمولكم، وبه احتج أبو حنيفة رحمه الله على عمرو بن عبيد. وفي حديث رواه الحاكم وصححه البيهقي من حديث حذيفة مرفوعاً: ((إن الله صانع كلَّ صانع وصنعته)) . ولذا وبخهم سبحانه بقوله تعالى: ﴿اتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ ﴾ [الصفت : ٩٥] أي ما تعملون من الأصنام، وبقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَنْ يَخْلُقُ كَمَنْ لَا يَخْلُقُ [النحل:١٧]، ولأن العبد لو كان خالقاً لأفعاله لكان عالماً بتفاصيلها كما يشير إليه سبحانه بقوله: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ [الملك: ١٤]، وقول علي كرم الله تعالى وجهه: عرفت الله بفسخ العزائم»، ولقد أغرب المعتزلة حيث صرفوا قوله تعالى: ﴿ اللهُ خَالِقُ كُلّ شَيْء [الزمر: ٦٢] إلى صفة الله حتى قالوا: إن كلامه مخلوق، ولم يصرفوه إلى صفات الخلق حتى قالوا: إن أفعال العباد غير مخلوقة له.
(And Allah, Exalted is He, is the Creator of them) i.e., the Originator of the actions of the servants according to what He willed, due to His saying, Exalted is He: {Allah is the Creator of everything} [Az-Zumar: 62], i.e., of every possible thing by the indication of reason, and the servant's action is a thing. And due to His saying, Exalted is He: {Is He who creates like one who does not create?} [An-Nahl: 17], i.e., the one from whom the reality of creation issues is not like the one from whom that does not issue in anything. And this is in the context of praising Himself with creatorhood and it being a cause for deserving worship. And due to His saying, Exalted is He: {And Allah created you and what you do} [As-Saffat: 96], i.e., your work or your work-product, and with this Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, argued against 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. And in a hadith narrated by al-Hakim and authenticated by al-Bayhaqi from Hudhayfa, marfu': 'Indeed Allah is the maker of every maker and his handiwork.' Therefore He, exalted, rebuked them with His saying: {Do you worship what you carve?} [As-Saffat: 95], i.e., what you make of idols, and with His saying: {Is He who creates like one who does not create?} [An-Nahl: 17]. And because if the servant were the creator of his actions, he would be knowledgeable of their details, as He, exalted, indicates by His saying: {Does He who create not know?} [Al-Mulk: 14], and the saying of 'Ali, may Allah ennoble his face: 'I knew Allah by the breaking of resolutions.' And indeed the Mu'tazila have gone far astray where they diverted His saying, Exalted is He: {Allah is the Creator of everything} to the attributes of Allah, so that they said: His speech is created, and they did not divert it to the attributes of creation, so that they said: the actions of the servants are not created by Him.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a set of proofs that Allah creates all human actions. The author begins by explaining the lemma 'والله تعالى خالقها' meaning Allah is the originator of the actions of the servants according to His will. He provides several pieces of evidence: 1) The verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' – the action of the servant is a 'thing', so Allah creates it. 2) The verse 'Is He who creates like one who does not create?' – this is in the context of praising His creatorhood as a basis for worship. 3) The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' – Abu Hanifa used this against 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. 4) A hadith 'Indeed Allah is the maker of every maker and his handiwork.' 5) The rebuke in the verses about worshipping carved idols. 6) A rational argument: if the servant were the creator of his actions, he would know their details, but he does not, as indicated by 'Does He who create not know?' and the saying of Ali. Then the author criticizes the Mu'tazila for misinterpreting the verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' to refer only to the attributes (like created speech) and not to the actions of servants, thereby denying that actions are created by Allah.

خلق
صانع
صنعة
خالقية
صفات الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe that the verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' applies only to attributes (like created speech) and does not include human actions.
Correction: The verse is general and includes the actions of servants because they are 'things'. The Mu'tazila inconsistency is clear: they apply it to attributes but not to actions.

Checkpoint
What proof does Abu Hanifa use against 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd according to the passage?
A) The verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything'
B) The verse 'Allah created you and what you do'
C) The hadith 'Allah is the maker of every maker'
D) The saying of 'Ali about breaking resolutions

Key Takeaway
Allah creates all human actions, as proven by multiple Quranic verses, a hadith, and rational argument; the Mu'tazila error is to exclude actions from Allah's creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah creates every action you perform, including your sins and your good deeds, how does that reshape your understanding of your own responsibility? Does it make you more or less accountable before Him?
?
When you make plans for tomorrow, do you genuinely acknowledge that Allah will create every step you take, or do you unconsciously act as if you are the independent author of your own life? What one habit could you change today to live more in light of this truth?
?
The Mu'tazila twisted a clear verse to avoid attributing human actions to Allah. Are there any areas of your belief or practice where you subtly resist Allah's absolute control—perhaps in moments of pride over your achievements or despair over your failures? Will you repent of that hidden independence right now?

Divine Attributes
