Misconception: Seeing Allah must involve facing Him or imply a location.
Correction: The vision of Allah is real but without direction; the moon hadith compares the clarity of vision, not the object.

Allah will be seen clearly in the afterlife, but without any direction or location, contrary to what some rationalists claim.

Knowing Allah Through His Self-Description
The author states that we know Allah only through His self-description in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct approach to knowing Allah according to the Salaf: through His self-description in the Quran, not by attempting to comprehend His essence, and the permissibility of using terms like 'nafs' and 'dhat' for Allah.

Core Idea
We know Allah only as He describes Himself; His essence is beyond comprehension.

This passage presents the foundational principle for knowing Allah: we know Him solely through His own description in the Quran, with all His attributes, to the extent of our human capacity. It also addresses the permissibility of applying certain terms to Allah, such as 'nafs' (self) and 'dhat' (essence), and clarifies a common misunderstanding regarding a hadith about pondering Allah's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Pay attention to the key terms 'nafs' and 'dhat'.
2
Identify the main principle
The author states we know Allah as He described Himself, not by comprehending His essence. Note the phrase 'بجميع صفاته' (with all His attributes).
This principle guards against trying to know Allah beyond revelation.
3
Examine the evidence for 'nafs'
Notice that the phrase 'كما وصف نفسه' is used as evidence that 'nafs' can be applied to Allah's essence. Understand the reasoning.
4
Understand the discussion on 'dhat'
The author presents the hadith 'تفكروا في كل شيء ولا تفكروا في ذات الله' and then critiques al-Suyuti's claim that 'dhat' appears in Bukhari.
Pay attention to the two objections: it's a Companion's statement, and the context suggests 'in the way of Allah'.
5
Reflect on the balance
Reflect on how this teaching maintains divine transcendence while affirming attributes, and how it guides our speech about Allah.
This connects to broader 'aqeedah principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعرف الله تعالى حق معرفته كما وصف نفسه في كتابه بجميع صفاته. نعرف الله تعالى حق (معرفته أي لا باعتبار كنه ذاته وإحاطة صفاته، بل بحسب مقدور العبد وطاقته في جميع حالاته (كما وصف أي الله سبحانه (نفسه) أي ذاته، وفيه دليل على جواز إطلاق النفس على ذاته تعالى. وأما إطلاق الذات فأكثر العلماء في العبارات جمعوا بين الذات والصفات، وقد ورد: ((تفكّروا في كل شيء ولا تفكروا في ذات الله)). (۱) وأما ما ذكره السيوطي من أنه قد ورد إطلاق الذات عليه سبحانه في البخاري في قصة وهو قوله: «وذلك في ذات الإله». ففيه بحث من وجهين : أما أولا فلأنه كلام صحابي، وأما ثانيا فلأنه ليس نصاً في المدعى بل الظاهر أنه أراد في سبيل الله.
We know Allah, the Exalted, the true knowledge of Him, as He described Himself in His Book with all His attributes. We know Allah, the Exalted, the true (knowledge of Him), i.e., not by way of the essence of His Self (kunh dhatihi) and encompassing His attributes, but according to the capacity and ability of the servant in all his states. (As He described) i.e., Allah, the Glorious, (Himself) i.e., His Essence (dhat). And in this is evidence for the permissibility of applying 'nafs' (self) to His Essence, the Exalted. As for applying 'dhat' (essence), most scholars in their expressions combine between the essence and the attributes. And it has been reported: 'Reflect on everything, but do not reflect on the Essence of Allah.' And as for what al-Suyuti mentioned, that the application of 'dhat' to Him, the Glorious, has occurred in al-Bukhari in a story, his saying: 'That is in the essence (dhat) of the deity.' There is discussion in two respects: Firstly, because it is the speech of a Companion; and secondly, because it is not a text for the claim, rather the apparent meaning is that he intended 'in the way of Allah (fi sabilillah).'
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the correct method of knowing Allah: we know Him as He described Himself in His Book, with all His attributes, both positive and negative. The author clarifies that this knowledge is not a comprehension of the essence (kunh dhat) nor an encompassing of attributes, but rather according to human capacity. The phrase 'as He described Himself' is used as evidence that it is permissible to apply the term 'nafs' (self) to Allah's essence. Then the author discusses the term 'dhat' (essence): it is used by many scholars, but there is a hadith warning against pondering the essence of Allah. Al-Suyuti claimed that the word 'dhat' appears in Sahih al-Bukhari in a report. The author critiques this claim on two grounds: first, the report is from a Companion, not the Prophet; second, the context suggests it means 'in the way of Allah' rather than the philosophical concept of essence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that knowing Allah as He described Himself means we can fully comprehend His essence and encompass all His attributes.
Correction: The author clarifies that we know Allah only according to our capacity, not by comprehending the essence or encompassing attributes.

Key Takeaway
The correct way to know Allah is through His Book and attributes, within human capacity, without attempting to comprehend His essence.

The Dispute Over 'Haqiqa' for Allah
Ibn al-Zamlakani and Ibn Jama'a oppose using 'haqiqa' for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why some scholars prohibit applying the term 'haqiqa' (reality) to Allah and the reasoning behind this position.

Core Idea
Applying 'haqiqa' to Allah is disputed because the term lacks scriptural warrant.

The term 'haqiqa' (reality) is commonly used in Islamic philosophy and theology to describe the essence of things. However, when it comes to Allah, scholars disagree on its permissibility. In this passage, we encounter a debate between Ibn al-Subki, who used it, and Ibn al-Zamlakani and Ibn Jama'a, who rejected it. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the three scholarly positions presented.
Note that the passage is concise; every phrase matters.
2
Identify the key figures
Ibn al-Subki is the one who initially used 'haqiqa' for Allah. Ibn al-Zamlakani objected, and Ibn Jama'a provided the reason.
3
Understand the objection
Ibn al-Zamlakani said it is prohibited (imtina') to apply the word 'haqiqa' to Allah. Ibn Jama'a clarified that this is because the term has not been reported in revelation.
The principle here is that theological language should be grounded in scripture.
4
Reflect on the methodological principle
Consider why scholars insist on scriptural evidence for describing Allah. This protects against speculative theology.
This connects to the broader Islamic emphasis on tawqif (stopping at revealed texts).

وأما إطلاق الحقيقة كما قال ابن السبكي في "جمع الجوامع": حقيقته مخالفة لسائر الحقائق، فأنكر عليه ابن الزملكاني حيث قال: يمتنع إطلاق لفظ الحقيقة على الله تعالى قال ابن جماعة: لأنه لم يرد.
As for applying 'haqiqa' (reality/essence), as Ibn al-Subki said in 'Jam' al-Jawami': 'His reality is contrary to all other realities.' So Ibn al-Zamlakani rejected this, saying: 'It is prohibited to apply the word haqiqa to Allah, the Exalted.' Ibn Jama'a said: 'Because it has not been reported (in revelation).'
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage discusses whether it is permissible to use the term 'haqiqa' (reality) for Allah. Ibn al-Subki asserted that Allah's 'haqiqa' is different from all other realities. However, Ibn al-Zamlakani strongly objected, stating that it is prohibited (imtina') to apply the term 'haqiqa' to Allah. The reason, as per Ibn Jama'a, is that this usage is not found in the Quran or hadith—i.e., it has no scriptural warrant. The passage thus reflects a disagreement among scholars: some allow it cautiously, while others forbid it because it implies a similarity to created things or because it is a term not used in revelation.

Key Terms
الحقيقة
ابن السبكي
ابن الزملكاني
ابن جماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'haqiqa' is a neutral, purely philosophical term that can be safely applied to Allah.
Correction: The passage shows that its use for Allah is controversial because it lacks scriptural basis; many scholars consider it prohibited.

Checkpoint
Why did Ibn Jama'a reject the use of 'haqiqa' for Allah?
A) Because it implies anthropomorphism
B) Because it has not been reported in revelation
C) Because it contradicts the Quran
D) Because it is a term used only for creation

Key Takeaway
The use of 'haqiqa' for Allah is rejected by some scholars because the term is not found in revelation, emphasizing the need for scriptural warrant in divine language.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about Allah, do you ever use words or concepts that you have not learned directly from the Quran or Sunnah? How might that lead to speaking about Allah without knowledge?
?
Are there attributes or descriptions of Allah that you commonly use in your prayers or conversations that have no basis in revelation? What is one such phrase you can commit to abandoning?
?
This lesson shows that even a word like 'haqiqa' is rejected because it is unrevealed. What does this teach you about the seriousness of guarding your tongue when it comes to Allah? Will you examine your own vocabulary about Allah and check it against the Quran and Sunnah starting today?

Permissible Terms for Allah
Discussion of permissible terms for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why only certain terms like nafs are permissible to apply to Allah, while others like haqiqah are not, based on revelation and scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
Divine terms are governed by revelation, not human speculation.

This passage begins the commentary by clarifying how we know Allah—not by comprehending His essence, but as He described Himself. It then examines three key terms (nafs, dhat, haqiqah) to demonstrate the principle that we must use only revealed or logically sanctioned language about Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the opening clarification about knowing Allah.
2
Identify the three terms discussed
Notice how each term (nafs, dhat, haqiqah) is evaluated.
3
Understand the reasoning
See the criteria used: evidence from revelation (for nafs), caution from hadith (for dhat), and lack of textual report (for haqiqah).
4
Reflect on the principle
Realize that theological language is rooted in revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعرف الله تعالى حق معرفته كما وصف نفسه في كتابه بجميع صفاته (أي لا باعتبار كنه ذاته وإحاطة صفاته، بل بحسب مقدور العبد وطاقته في جميع حالاته) كما وصف (أي الله سبحانه) نفسه (أي ذاته، وفيه دليل على جواز إطلاق النفس على ذاته تعالى. وأما إطلاق الذات فأكثر العلماء في العبارات جمعوا بين الذات والصفات، وقد ورد: ((تفكّروا في كل شيء ولا تفكروا في ذات الله)). وأما ما ذكره السيوطي من أنه قد ورد إطلاق الذات عليه سبحانه في البخاري في قصة وهو قوله: «وذلك في ذات الإله». ففيه بحث من وجهين: أما أولا فلأنه كلام صحابي، وأما ثانيا فلأنه ليس نصاً في المدعى بل الظاهر أنه أراد في سبيل الله، وذلك لأن الكفار لما خرجوا به من الحرم ليقتلوه قال: دعوني أصلي ركعتين، ثم أنشأ يقول: فلست أبالي حين أقتل مسلما على أي شق كان في الله مصرعي وذلك في ذات الإله وإن يشأ يبارك على أوصال شلو ممزع أي أعضاء جسد مقطع. وأما إطلاق الحقيقة كما قال ابن السبكي في "جمع الجوامع": حقيقته مخالفة لسائر الحقائق، فأنكر عليه ابن الزملكاني حيث قال: يمتنع إطلاق لفظ الحقيقة على الله تعالى قال ابن جماعة: لأنه لم يرد. متعلق بـ "وُصِفَ". في كتابه أي في مواضع من آياته بجميع صفاته أي الثبوتية والسلبية كسورة الإخلاص وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ ﴾ وسائر الآيات الدالة على تحقق الذات ومراتب الصفات، ولعل هذا الكلام من الإمام الهمام مبني على أن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص في حقيقة الإيقان وأنّ الإيمان الإجمالي كاف في مرام الإحسان فللمؤمن أن يقول عرفته. وأما قول من قال: ما عرفناك حق معرفتك، فمبني على أن إدراك الذات والإحاطة بكنه الصفات ليس في قدرة المخلوقات لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ ﴾ ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِهِ عِلْمًا ﴾ فاختلاف القضية بتفاوت الحيثية، ومن هنا قال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى: «من انتهض لطلب مدبّره فانتهى إلى موجود ينتهي إلى فكره فهو مشبه وإن اطمأن إلى العدم الصرف فهو معطل، وإن اطمأن إلى موجود فاعترف بالعجز عن إدراكه فهو موحد». ومن ثم لما سئل علي رضي الله عنه عن التوحيد ما معناه؟ فقال: أن تعلم أن ما خطر ببالك أو توهمته في خيالك أو تصوّرته في حال من أحوالك فالله تعالى وراء ذلك. ويرجع إلى هذا المعنى قول الجنيد رحمه الله تعالى: «التوحيد إفراد القدم من الحدوث»؛ إذ لا يخطر ببالك إلا حادث، فإفراد القدم أن لا تحكم على الله بمشابهة شيء من الموجودات لا في الذات ولا في الصفات بوجه من الوجوه، فإنه لا تشبه ذاته ذات ولا صفاته صفات. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ ﴾ بل ما جاء من إطلاق العالم والقادر والموجود وغير ذلك على القديم والحادث، فهو اشتراك لفظي فقط.
We know Allah Almighty with true knowledge as He described Himself in His Book with all His attributes (i.e., not by consideration of the reality of His essence and encompassing His attributes, but according to the capability and capacity of the servant in all his states) as He described (i.e., Allah Almighty) Himself (i.e., His essence, and in this is evidence for the permissibility of applying 'nafs' to His essence. As for applying 'dhat', most scholars in expressions combined between the essence and attributes, and it has been reported: 'Reflect on everything but do not reflect on the essence of Allah.' As for what al-Suyuti mentioned that the application of 'dhat' to Him has been reported in al-Bukhari in a story, namely his saying: 'That is concerning the essence of the deity' — there is discussion in it from two aspects: First, because it is the speech of a Companion; second, because it is not a clear text for the claim, but the apparent meaning is that he intended 'in the path of Allah', because when the disbelievers took him out of the sanctuary to kill him, he said: Let me pray two rak'ahs, then he recited: 'I do not care, when I am killed as a Muslim, upon which side I am killed in Allah's cause, and that is concerning the essence of the deity, and if He wills, He blesses the limbs of a torn body' i.e., the limbs of a cut-up body. As for applying 'haqiqah', as Ibn al-Subki said in 'Jam' al-Jawami': His reality is contrary to all other realities, but Ibn al-Zamalkani objected to him, saying: It is forbidden to apply the word 'haqiqah' to Allah Almighty; Ibn Jama'ah said: because it has not been reported. It is related to 'wasafa' (he described). 'In His Book' i.e., in places of His verses, with all His attributes, i.e., the affirmative and negative, like Surat al-Ikhlas and His saying: 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' and the rest of the verses indicating the reality of the essence and the degrees of attributes. Perhaps this speech from the imam is based on the fact that faith does not increase or decrease in the reality of certainty, and that summary faith is sufficient for the attainment of excellence, so the believer can say 'I know Him.' As for the saying of one who said: 'We have not known You with true knowledge,' it is based on the fact that comprehending the essence and encompassing the reality of attributes is not within the power of creatures, due to His saying: 'Vision perceives Him not' and His saying: 'But they encompass Him not in knowledge.' So the difference between the two statements is due to different perspectives. From here, Imam al-Shafi'i said: 'Whoever undertakes to seek his Director and ends at an existent that ends at his thought is a likener; if he is content with pure non-existence, he is a negator; and if he is content with an existent and admits inability to comprehend Him, he is a unitarian.' Hence, when 'Ali was asked about the meaning of tawhid, he said: That you know that whatever occurs to your mind or you imagine in your fantasy or picture in any state, Allah Almighty is beyond that. To this meaning refers the saying of al-Junayd: 'Tawhid is isolating the Pre-eternal from temporal origination'; for nothing occurs to your mind except a contingent thing. Isolating the Pre-eternal means that you do not judge Allah to resemble any of the existents, neither in essence nor in attributes in any way, for His essence resembles no essence and His attributes resemble no attributes. Allah said: 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing.' Rather, what has come of applying 'the Knowing', 'the Powerful', 'the Existent', and others to the Pre-eternal and the temporal is merely verbal commonality (ishtirak lafzi).
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary explaining the opening statement 'We know Allah with true knowledge as He described Himself in His Book with all His attributes.' The commentator clarifies that this knowledge is not an encompassing comprehension of Allah's essence or attributes, but rather a knowledge proportionate to the servant's capacity. He then discusses the permissibility of applying the term 'nafs' (self) to Allah, citing the verse 'as He described Himself' as evidence. The commentary then addresses the term 'dhat' (essence), noting that most scholars use both 'dhat' and 'sifat' together, and warns against reflecting on Allah's essence based on a hadith. It critiques al-Suyuti's claim that 'dhat' is applied to Allah in a hadith in al-Bukhari, arguing that the hadith is from a Companion and its context indicates it means 'in the path of Allah' rather than a literal application of 'dhat' to Allah. The commentary then discusses the term 'haqiqah' (reality), noting that Ibn al-Subki used it but was criticized by Ibn al-Zamalkani and Ibn Jama'ah because it is not reported in revelation. The commentator returns to explaining 'in His Book with all His attributes', dividing attributes into affirmative (thubutiyya) and negative (salbiyya), citing Surat al-Ikhlas and the verse 'There is nothing like unto Him...'. He then clarifies an apparent contradiction: some say 'I know Allah' while others say 'We have not known You with true knowledge.' The resolution is that the first statement refers to faith and certainty (summary knowledge is sufficient), while the second refers to grasping the essence and encompassing attributes, which is impossible. This leads to a discussion of tawhid, quoting al-Shafi'i's three categories: likener (tashbih), negator (ta'til), and the true monotheist who affirms existence while admitting inability to comprehend. The passage then cites 'Ali's definition of tawhid as knowing that Allah is beyond any mental image, and al-Junayd's definition as isolating the Pre-eternal from temporal origination. It concludes that terms like 'Knower', 'Powerful', 'Existent' when applied to both Creator and creatures are merely verbal homonyms (ishtirak lafzi), not implying any similarity.

Key Terms
النفس
الذات
الحقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can apply any philosophical term to Allah, like 'haqiqah', if it seems logically appropriate.
Correction: Ibn Jama'ah clarifies that the term 'haqiqah' is not applied to Allah because it has not been reported in revelation (lam yarid).

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the term 'haqiqah' (reality) not applied to Allah?
A) Because it implies a comparison with other realities
B) Because it has not been reported in revelation
C) Because Allah's reality is unknowable
D) Because it is a philosophical term

Key Takeaway
Only terms sanctioned by revelation or scholarly consensus can be applied to Allah; unapproved terms like 'haqiqah' are rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever describe Allah with terms you have not heard from the Quran or Sunnah? How can you ensure your words about Allah are always based on revelation, not your own reasoning?
?
When you say you 'know Allah', do you secretly assume you have comprehended His essence? This lesson says we know Him only as He described Himself. What pride in your knowledge must you repent of?
?
The Companion recited poetry in the face of death, using a term that later scholars rejected. What does your comfort with using unapproved terms say about your reverence for Allah's transcendence? Will you commit to learning only divinely taught names?

Affirmative and Negative Attributes
Explanation of affirmative and negative attributes and the limits of human knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between affirmative and negative attributes, and how summary faith is sufficient while comprehensive knowledge of Allah's essence is impossible.

Core Idea
We affirm all attributes without trying to grasp their reality.

After establishing permissible terms, the commentary turns to the attributes themselves. It explains that the attributes are either affirmative or negative, and that the Quran contains both types. Then it addresses an apparent contradiction: some say 'I know Allah' while others say 'We have not known You with true knowledge.' The resolution lies in distinguishing between summary faith and comprehensive knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on attributes
Notice the division into thubutiyya (affirmative) and salbiyya (negative) attributes.
2
Understand the resolution
See that summary faith (iman ijmail) is sufficient for salvation, while full comprehension is impossible.
3
Connect to the Quran
The verses cited show both affirmation and negation.

We know Allah Almighty with true knowledge as He described Himself in His Book with all His attributes (i.e., not by consideration of the reality of His essence and encompassing His attributes, but according to the capability and capacity of the servant in all his states) as He described (i.e., Allah Almighty) Himself (i.e., His essence, and in this is evidence for the permissibility of applying 'nafs' to His essence. Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary explaining the opening statement 'We know Allah with true knowledge as He described Himself in His Book with all His attributes.' The commentator clarifies that this knowledge is not an encompassing comprehension of Allah's essence or attributes, but rather a knowledge proportionate to the servant's capacity. He then discusses the permissibility of applying the term 'nafs' (self) to Allah, citing the verse 'as He described Himself' as evidence. The commentary then addresses the term 'dhat' (essence), noting that most scholars use both 'dhat' and 'sifat' together, and warns against reflecting on Allah's essence based on a hadith. It critiques al-Suyuti's claim that 'dhat' is applied to Allah in a hadith in al-Bukhari, arguing that the hadith is from a Companion and its context indicates it means 'in the path of Allah' rather than a literal application of 'dhat' to Allah. The commentary then discusses the term 'haqiqah' (reality), noting that Ibn al-Subki used it but was criticized by Ibn al-Zamalkani and Ibn Jama'ah because it is not reported in revelation. The commentator returns to explaining 'in His Book with all His attributes', dividing attributes into affirmative (thubutiyya) and negative (salbiyya), citing Surat al-Ikhlas and the verse 'There is nothing like unto Him...'. He then clarifies an apparent contradiction: some say 'I know Allah' while others say 'We have not known You with true knowledge.' The resolution is that the first statement refers to faith and certainty (summary knowledge is sufficient), while the second refers to grasping the essence and encompassing attributes, which is impossible. This leads to a discussion of tawhid, quoting al-Shafi'i's three categories: likener (tashbih), negator (ta'til), and the true monotheist who affirms existence while admitting inability to comprehend. The passage then cites 'Ali's definition of tawhid as knowing that Allah is beyond any mental image, and al-Junayd's definition as isolating the Pre-eternal from temporal origination. It concludes that terms like 'Knower', 'Powerful', 'Existent' when applied to both Creator and creatures are merely verbal homonyms (ishtirak lafzi), not implying any similarity.

Key Terms
الصفات الثبوتية
الصفات السلبية
الإيمان الإجمالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith increases or decreases in certainty, and one cannot claim to know Allah unless they comprehend Him fully.
Correction: The passage states that faith does not increase or decrease in the reality of certainty, and summary faith is sufficient; the statement 'we have not known You' refers not to faith but to comprehensive knowledge of essence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do some people say 'We have not known You with true knowledge'?
A) Because they lack faith
B) Because comprehending the essence is impossible for creatures
C) Because they are negators
D) Because they use wrong terms

Key Takeaway
We affirm all of Allah's attributes as revealed, but acknowledge that our knowledge is limited and cannot encompass His essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your knowledge of Allah is sufficient even though you cannot fully comprehend Him, or does the uncertainty make you uneasy? Will you submit to the limits He has placed on your understanding?
?
When you recite Allah's attributes, are you satisfied with affirming them as revealed, or do you find yourself trying to imagine 'how' He sees or hears? Will you repent from such attempts and accept His transcendence?
?
If you were asked today, 'Do you know your Lord?' would you answer with the certainty of summary faith, or would your hesitation reveal a hidden reliance on your own intellect? Will you commit to believing without demanding full comprehension?

Three Categories of Tawhid and Homonyms
Classification of tawhid and the principle of verbal commonality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize the three approaches to the Divine (tashbih, ta'til, tawhid) and understand that terms applied to Allah and creation are merely verbal homonyms.

Core Idea
True tawhid is affirming Allah's existence while denying any resemblance to creation.

The commentary culminates with a powerful classification by Imam al-Shafi'i of three types of people: those who liken Allah to creation, those who negate His existence, and the true monotheists who affirm His existence while admitting their inability to comprehend Him. This leads to definitions of tawhid by Ali and al-Junayd, and concludes with the principle that shared terms like 'Knower' are only verbal homonyms, not implying similarity.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Shafi'i's three categories
Identify each category and its error/correctness.
2
Reflect on Ali's definition
What does it mean that Allah is beyond any mental image?
3
Grasp al-Junayd's definition
Tawhid is isolating the Pre-eternal from temporal.
4
Learn the conclusion
Terms applied to Allah and creation are homonyms.

نعرف الله تعالى حق معرفته كما وصف نفسه في كتابه بجميع صفاته (أي لا باعتبار كنه ذاته وإحاطة صفاته، بل بحسب مقدور العبد وطاقته في جميع حالاته) كما وصف (أي الله سبحانه) نفسه (أي ذاته، وفيه دليل على جواز إطلاق النفس على ذاته تعالى. وأما إطلاق الذات فأكثر العلماء في العبارات جمعوا بين الذات والصفات، وقد ورد: ((تفكّروا في كل شيء ولا تفكروا في ذات الله)). وأما ما ذكره السيوطي من أنه قد ورد إطلاق الذات عليه سبحانه في البخاري في قصة وهو قوله: «وذلك في ذات الإله». ففيه بحث من وجهين: أما أولا فلأنه كلام صحابي، وأما ثانيا فلأنه ليس نصاً في المدعى بل الظاهر أنه أراد في سبيل الله، وذلك لأن الكفار لما خرجوا به من الحرم ليقتلوه قال: دعوني أصلي ركعتين، ثم أنشأ يقول: فلست أبالي حين أقتل مسلما على أي شق كان في الله مصرعي وذلك في ذات الإله وإن يشأ يبارك على أوصال شلو ممزع أي أعضاء جسد مقطع. وأما إطلاق الحقيقة كما قال ابن السبكي في "جمع الجوامع": حقيقته مخالفة لسائر الحقائق، فأنكر عليه ابن الزملكاني حيث قال: يمتنع إطلاق لفظ الحقيقة على الله تعالى قال ابن جماعة: لأنه لم يرد. متعلق بـ "وُصِفَ". في كتابه أي في مواضع من آياته بجميع صفاته أي الثبوتية والسلبية كسورة الإخلاص وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ ﴾ وسائر الآيات الدالة على تحقق الذات ومراتب الصفات، ولعل هذا الكلام من الإمام الهمام مبني على أن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص في حقيقة الإيقان وأنّ الإيمان الإجمالي كاف في مرام الإحسان فللمؤمن أن يقول عرفته. وأما قول من قال: ما عرفناك حق معرفتك، فمبني على أن إدراك الذات والإحاطة بكنه الصفات ليس في قدرة المخلوقات لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ ﴾ ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِهِ عِلْمًا ﴾ فاختلاف القضية بتفاوت الحيثية، ومن هنا قال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى: «من انتهض لطلب مدبّره فانتهى إلى موجود ينتهي إلى فكره فهو مشبه وإن اطمأن إلى العدم الصرف فهو معطل، وإن اطمأن إلى موجود فاعترف بالعجز عن إدراكه فهو موحد». ومن ثم لما سئل علي رضي الله عنه عن التوحيد ما معناه؟ فقال: أن تعلم أن ما خطر ببالك أو توهمته في خيالك أو تصوّرته في حال من أحوالك فالله تعالى وراء ذلك. ويرجع إلى هذا المعنى قول الجنيد رحمه الله تعالى: «التوحيد إفراد القدم من الحدوث»؛ إذ لا يخطر ببالك إلا حادث، فإفراد القدم أن لا تحكم على الله بمشابهة شيء من الموجودات لا في الذات ولا في الصفات بوجه من الوجوه، فإنه لا تشبه ذاته ذات ولا صفاته صفات. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ ﴾ بل ما جاء من إطلاق العالم والقادر والموجود وغير ذلك على القديم والحادث، فهو اشتراك لفظي فقط.
We know Allah Almighty with true knowledge as He described Himself in His Book with all His attributes (i.e., not by consideration of the reality of His essence and encompassing His attributes, but according to the capability and capacity of the servant in all his states) as He described (i.e., Allah Almighty) Himself (i.e., His essence, and in this is evidence for the permissibility of applying 'nafs' to His essence. As for applying 'dhat', most scholars in expressions combined between the essence and attributes, and it has been reported: 'Reflect on everything but do not reflect on the essence of Allah.' As for what al-Suyuti mentioned that the application of 'dhat' to Him has been reported in al-Bukhari in a story, namely his saying: 'That is concerning the essence of the deity' — there is discussion in it from two aspects: First, because it is the speech of a Companion; second, because it is not a clear text for the claim, but the apparent meaning is that he intended 'in the path of Allah', because when the disbelievers took him out of the sanctuary to kill him, he said: Let me pray two rak'ahs, then he recited: 'I do not care, when I am killed as a Muslim, upon which side I am killed in Allah's cause, and that is concerning the essence of the deity, and if He wills, He blesses the limbs of a torn body' i.e., the limbs of a cut-up body. As for applying 'haqiqah', as Ibn al-Subki said in 'Jam' al-Jawami': His reality is contrary to all other realities, but Ibn al-Zamalkani objected to him, saying: It is forbidden to apply the word 'haqiqah' to Allah Almighty; Ibn Jama'ah said: because it has not been reported. It is related to 'wasafa' (he described). 'In His Book' i.e., in places of His verses, with all His attributes, i.e., the affirmative and negative, like Surat al-Ikhlas and His saying: 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' and the rest of the verses indicating the reality of the essence and the degrees of attributes. Perhaps this speech from the imam is based on the fact that faith does not increase or decrease in the reality of certainty, and that summary faith is sufficient for the attainment of excellence, so the believer can say 'I know Him.' As for the saying of one who said: 'We have not known You with true knowledge,' it is based on the fact that comprehending the essence and encompassing the reality of attributes is not within the power of creatures, due to His saying: 'Vision perceives Him not' and His saying: 'But they encompass Him not in knowledge.' So the difference between the two statements is due to different perspectives. From here, Imam al-Shafi'i said: 'Whoever undertakes to seek his Director and ends at an existent that ends at his thought is a likener; if he is content with pure non-existence, he is a negator; and if he is content with an existent and admits inability to comprehend Him, he is a unitarian.' Hence, when 'Ali was asked about the meaning of tawhid, he said: That you know that whatever occurs to your mind or you imagine in your fantasy or picture in any state, Allah Almighty is beyond that. To this meaning refers the saying of al-Junayd: 'Tawhid is isolating the Pre-eternal from temporal origination'; for nothing occurs to your mind except a contingent thing. Isolating the Pre-eternal means that you do not judge Allah to resemble any of the existents, neither in essence nor in attributes in any way, for His essence resembles no essence and His attributes resemble no attributes. Allah said: 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing.' Rather, what has come of applying 'the Knowing', 'the Powerful', 'the Existent', and others to the Pre-eternal and the temporal is merely verbal commonality (ishtirak lafzi).

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary explaining the opening statement 'We know Allah with true knowledge as He described Himself in His Book with all His attributes.' The commentator clarifies that this knowledge is not an encompassing comprehension of Allah's essence or attributes, but rather a knowledge proportionate to the servant's capacity. He then discusses the permissibility of applying the term 'nafs' (self) to Allah, citing the verse 'as He described Himself' as evidence. The commentary then addresses the term 'dhat' (essence), noting that most scholars use both 'dhat' and 'sifat' together, and warns against reflecting on Allah's essence based on a hadith. It critiques al-Suyuti's claim that 'dhat' is applied to Allah in a hadith in al-Bukhari, arguing that the hadith is from a Companion and its context indicates it means 'in the path of Allah' rather than a literal application of 'dhat' to Allah. The commentary then discusses the term 'haqiqah' (reality), noting that Ibn al-Subki used it but was criticized by Ibn al-Zamalkani and Ibn Jama'ah because it is not reported in revelation. The commentator returns to explaining 'in His Book with all His attributes', dividing attributes into affirmative (thubutiyya) and negative (salbiyya), citing Surat al-Ikhlas and the verse 'There is nothing like unto Him...'. He then clarifies an apparent contradiction: some say 'I know Allah' while others say 'We have not known You with true knowledge.' The resolution is that the first statement refers to faith and certainty (summary knowledge is sufficient), while the second refers to grasping the essence and encompassing attributes, which is impossible. This leads to a discussion of tawhid, quoting al-Shafi'i's three categories: likener (tashbih), negator (ta'til), and the true monotheist who affirms existence while admitting inability to comprehend. The passage then cites 'Ali's definition of tawhid as knowing that Allah is beyond any mental image, and al-Junayd's definition as isolating the Pre-eternal from temporal origination. It concludes that terms like 'Knower', 'Powerful', 'Existent' when applied to both Creator and creatures are merely verbal homonyms (ishtirak lafzi), not implying any similarity.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because we use the same words for God and humans (e.g., 'knowing', 'powerful'), God's knowledge and power are similar to ours.
Correction: The passage states that such terms are merely verbal commonality (ishtirak lafzi), meaning they share a name but not a reality.

God's Grace and Justice and Multiplied Reward
The commentator explains God's grace and justice and that He gives multiplied reward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God is both bestowing favor and just, and that He gives reward far beyond what is deserved as a grace.

Core Idea
God's grace gives multiplied reward beyond justice.

This passage from the commentary explains two key divine attributes: that God is bestowing favor (mutafaḍḍil) and just (ʿādil). It clarifies that God acts with grace towards some and justice towards others, and emphasizes that multiplied reward is a favor, not a strict obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let the text speak for itself before analyzing.
Notice the use of Quranic verses and hadith to support the points.
2
Identify the two attributes
Find the two attributes 'bestowing favor' (mutafaḍḍil) and 'just' (ʿādil). Understand how they are defined in the context.
The commentator distinguishes between grace and justice actions.
3
Reflect on the quoted texts
Consider the Quranic verses (10:25 and 2:261) and the sacred hadith. What do they teach about God's will and reward?
The hadith emphasizes God's absolute sovereignty in creation.
4
Grasp the concept of multiplied reward
Understand that the multiplied reward is a favor (tafaḍḍul) from God, not a mandatory payment. It is connected to sincerity (ikhlāṣ).
This shows God's generosity beyond justice.

والله تعالى متفضل على عباده أي عامل بفضله على بعضهم (عادل) أي عامل بعدله في بعضهم كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللهُ يَدْعُوا إِلَى دَارِ السَّلَامِ وَيَهْدِى مَنْ يَشَاءُ إِلَى صِرَاطٍ مُّسْتَقِيمٍ [يونس: ٢٥]، وفي الحديث القدسي: ((خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ولا أبالي، وخلقت هؤلاء للنار ولا أبالي)) . (١) وهذا باعتبار توفيق الإيمان وتحقيق الخذلان ويترتب عليه قوله (قد يعطي) أي الله سبحانه من (الثواب) أي الأجر على الطاعة في الدنيا والآخرة أضعاف ما يستوجبه العبد) أي يستحق تفضلا منه أي في الزيادة كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللهُ يُضْعِفُ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٦١] ، أي ما يشاء من الدرجات في المثوبة ومقام القربة بحسب الإخلاص.
And Allah the Exalted is bestowing favor (mutafaḍḍil) upon His servants: i.e., acting with His grace towards some of them. 'Just' (ʿādil): i.e., acting with His justice towards some of them, as Allah the Exalted said: 'And Allah invites to the abode of peace and guides whom He wills to a straight path' [Q 10:25], and in the sacred hadith: 'I created these for Paradise and I do not care, and I created these for the Fire and I do not care.' This is with regard to granting success for faith and causing abandonment. And upon it follows His statement 'He may give' (qad yuʿṭī): i.e., Allah the Glorified gives of reward, i.e., recompense for obedience in this world and the next, multiples of what the servant deserves, i.e., is entitled to, as a favor from Him, i.e., in increase, as Allah the Exalted said: 'And Allah multiplies for whom He wills' [Q 2:261], i.e., whatever He wills of degrees in reward and the station of closeness according to sincerity.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of two divine attributes mentioned in the original text: 'bestowing favor' (mutafaḍḍil) and 'just' (ʿādil). The commentator explains that God acts with grace towards some servants and with justice towards others, quoting Quran 10:25 which shows God guides whom He wills. He then cites a sacred hadith that God created some for Paradise and some for Fire without concern, indicating that guidance and abandonment are by His will. The commentator clarifies that this relates to granting success for faith and causing abandonment. Then he addresses the statement 'He may give reward in multiples of what the servant deserves', explaining that God gives reward far beyond what is deserved, as a favor. This is supported by Quran 2:261 where Allah says He multiplies for whom He wills. The multiplication is in degrees of reward and closeness according to sincerity.

عدل (ʿadl)
الثواب (al-thawāb)
أضعاف (aḍʿāf)
استوجب (istawjaba)
الإخلاص (al-ikhlāṣ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's justice means He must treat everyone equally without any extra favor.
Correction: The passage shows that God gives multiplied reward as a grace, not as a requirement of justice.

Key Takeaway
God gives multiplied reward as a grace beyond what is deserved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

God's Grace and Justice in Reward and Punishment
The commentator explains God's attributes of grace and justice in giving reward and punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's attributes of grace and justice are reflected in His giving of reward, punishment, and forgiveness.

Core Idea
God's grace gives more than deserved; His justice gives exactly what is due.

In this passage, the commentator explains two fundamental divine attributes — grace (tafaḍḍul) and justice (ʿadl) — as they apply to reward, punishment, and forgiveness. Before we can grasp Islamic teachings on divine recompense, we must see how these attributes work together without contradiction. This commentary clarifies that any increase beyond exact requital is pure grace, and any forgiveness is sheer mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two attributes
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins by affirming that God is 'gracious' (mutafaḍḍil) and 'just' (ʿādil). These are the key attributes that shape the rest.
The passage cites a verse and a hadith to support this.
2
Focus on reward as grace
The commentator explains that reward (thawāb) is given in multiples beyond what the servant deserves, citing the verse 'And God multiplies for whom He wills'. This is an act of grace.
3
Focus on punishment as justice
Punishment is described as exactly proportionate to the sin, no increase. The verse from al-Anʿām is quoted to show that good deeds are multiplied tenfold but evil deeds are requited only with their like.
This demonstrates God's justice.
4
Focus on forgiveness as grace
Forgiveness (ʿafw) is also an act of grace, whether through intercession or directly. Two verses are cited showing God's pardon.
5
Summarize the conclusion
The commentator concludes that the tenfold multiplication is general for all good deeds, while any increase beyond that is specific and special, all being pure grace and mercy.
This ties together the themes of grace and justice.

والله تعالى متفضل على عباده أي عامل بفضله على بعضهم (عادل) أي عامل بعدله في بعضهم كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللهُ يَدْعُوا إِلَى دَارِ السَّلَامِ وَيَهْدِى مَنْ يَشَاءُ إِلَى صِرَاطٍ مُّسْتَقِيمٍ ﴾ [يونس: ٢٥]، وفي الحديث القدسي: ((خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ولا أبالي، وخلقت هؤلاء للنار ولا أبالي)) . (۱) وهذا باعتبار توفيق الإيمان وتحقيق الخذلان ويترتب عليه قوله (قد يعطي) أي الله سبحانه من (الثواب) أي الأجر على الطاعة في الدنيا والآخرة أضعاف ما يستوجبه العبد) أي يستحق تفضلا منه أي في الزيادة كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللهُ يُضْعِفُ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٦١] ، أي ما يشاء من الدرجات في المثوبة ومقام القربة بحسب الإخلاص. وقد يعاقب على (الذنب أي بقدر ما يستحقه العبد بلا زيادة عقوبة عدلا منه كما أخبر عنها في كتابه بقوله تعالى: مَنْ جَاءَ بِالْحَسَنَةِ فَلَهُ عَشْرُ أَمْثَالِهَا وَ مَنْ جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَلَا يُجْزَى إِلَّا مِثْلَهَا وَهُمْ لَا يُظْلَمُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٦٠]، أي بنقص ثواب أو بزيادة عقاب (وقد يعفو) أي عن السيئة فضلا منه سواء يكون بواسطة شفاعة أو بدونها لقوله سبحانه وتعالى: وَمَا أَصَابَكُمْ مِنْ مُّصِيبَةٍ فَبِمَا كَسَبَتْ أَيْدِيكُمْ وَيَعْفُوا عَنْ كَثِيرن ﴾ [الشورى: ۳۰] ، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النساء : ٤٨] ، أي ما دون الشرك صغيرا أو كبيرا لمن يريد غفرانه تفضلا. والحاصل أن زيادة العشرة عامة، وأما الزيادة عليها فخاصة والكل فضل محض ورحمة خالصة.
And God Most High is gracious to His servants, meaning He acts with His grace towards some of them, (just) meaning He acts with His justice towards some of them, as God said: 'And God calls to the abode of peace and guides whom He wills to a straight path' [Yunus: 25], and in the sacred hadith: 'I created these for Paradise and I care not, and I created these for the Fire and I care not.' This is with regard to granting success in faith and effecting abandonment. It follows that He said: 'He may give'—that is, God— from 'reward', meaning recompense for obedience in this world and the Hereafter, multiples of what the servant deserves, meaning merits, as a grace from Him, i.e., in increase, as God said: 'And God multiplies for whom He wills' [Al-Baqarah: 261], meaning whatever He wills of degrees in recompense and station of nearness according to sincerity. And He may punish for sin, meaning to the extent that the servant deserves without increase in punishment, as justice from Him, as He informed about it in His book by His saying: 'Whoever comes with a good deed shall have ten times its like, and whoever comes with an evil deed shall not be recompensed except with its like, and they shall not be wronged' [Al-An'am: 160], meaning by decrease of reward or increase of punishment. And He may forgive, meaning the evil deed, out of His grace, whether through intercession or without it, because of His statement: 'And whatever misfortune befalls you, it is because of what your hands have earned, and He pardons much' [Ash-Shura: 30], and His statement: 'And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [An-Nisa: 48], meaning what is less than shirk, small or great, for whom He desires its forgiveness as a grace. The conclusion is that the multiplication by ten is general, and the increase beyond that is specific, and all is pure grace and pure mercy.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of two divine attributes: grace (tafaḍḍul) and justice (ʿadl). The commentator first states that God is gracious to His servants (mutafaḍḍil) by acting with His grace towards some, and just (ʿādil) by acting with justice towards others, citing a Qur'anic verse about God's guidance and a sacred hadith about predestination. Then he explains the phrase 'He may give' (qad yuʿṭī) — that God gives reward for obedience multiplied beyond what the servant deserves, as a grace, with the example from the Qur'an that God multiplies for whom He wills. Next, he explains 'He may punish' (qad yuʿāqib) on sin — that God punishes exactly to the extent deserved, no more, as justice, citing the verse that good deeds are multiplied tenfold but evil deeds are requited only with their like. Finally, he explains 'He may forgive' (qad yaʿfū) — that God forgives sins out of grace, whether through intercession or not, citing two verses about God's forgiveness. The concluding summary (al-ḥāṣil) notes that the tenfold multiplication is general for all good deeds, but additional increase beyond that is specific to those God wills, and all is pure grace and mercy.

ثواب

مثوبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's justice means equal reward for equal deeds, so any increase is unjust.
Correction: The passage clarifies that any increase beyond exact equivalent is a free act of grace (tafaḍḍul), not a violation of justice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for punishment from God?
A) It is strictly proportionate to the sin as an act of justice
B) It is always multiplied like reward
C) It is always forgiven out of grace
D) It is arbitrary

Key Takeaway
God's reward multiplies beyond merit by grace; His punishment is exact justice; His forgiveness is pure grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every good deed you do is rewarded by God beyond what you deserve, or do you feel entitled to reward? How does this affect your sincerity in worship?
?
When you commit a sin, do you expect God to punish you exactly, or do you hope for His forgiveness? Does your hope in His grace lead you to repentance or to complacency?
?
The lesson says forgiveness is pure grace. Is there a sin you think is too big for God to forgive? How does this lesson challenge that assumption and your relationship with His mercy?

Punishment as Justice: Proportional Recompense
Definition and proof of punishment as justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's punishment is an act of justice ('adl) because it is exactly proportionate to the sin, without any increase beyond what is deserved.

Core Idea
God's punishment is perfectly just: no more than what is deserved.

The commentator begins by clarifying the nature of divine punishment, grounding it in justice. He explains that when God punishes, He gives exactly what the servant deserves, no more. This lesson examines that key principle and the Quranic evidence supporting it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on punishment
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the key term 'عدل' (justice) and how it is defined.
The definition of 'عدل' here is 'بقدر ما يستحقه العبد بلا زيادة عقوبة'.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Locate the verse from Surat al-An'am (6:160) and understand how it supports the idea of proportional recompense.
The verse promises ten rewards for good and exactly one like for evil, implying no excess.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: Why is it important that punishment is 'without increase'? How does this relate to God's justice?
This assures that God never wrongs His servants by punishing beyond what they deserve.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يعاقب على الذنب عدلا منه وقد يعفو فضلا منه. وقد يعاقب على الذنب أي بقدر ما يستحقه العبد بلا زيادة عقوبة عدلا منه كما أخبر عنها في كتابه بقوله تعالى: ﴿مَنْ جَاءَ بِالْحَسَنَةِ فَلَهُ عَشْرُ أَمْثَالِهَا وَمَنْ جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَلَا يُجْزَى إِلَّا مِثْلَهَا وَهُمْ لَا يُظْلَمُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٦٠]، أي بنقص ثواب أو بزيادة عقاب. وقد يعفو أي عن السيئة فضلا منه سواء يكون بواسطة شفاعة أو بدونها لقوله سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَصَابَكُمْ مِنْ مُصِيبَةٍ فَبِمَا كَسَبَتْ أَيْدِيكُمْ وَيَعْفُو عَنْ كَثِيرٍ﴾ [الشورى: ٣٠]، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ﴾ [النساء: ٤٨]، أي ما دون الشرك صغيرا أو كبيرا لمن يريد غفرانه تفضلا. والحاصل أن زيادة العشرة عامة، وأما الزيادة عليها فخاصة والكل فضل محض ورحمة خالصة، وربما تكون الزيادة بسبب اختلاف مقامات أصحاب العبادة أو بحسب تعلق مجرد الإرادة بما سبق لهم من عناية السعادة. وأما قول شارح: «فليس له أن يعطي من الثواب أحد المتساويين في العبادة واليقين أكثر مما يعطي الآخر، أو يعفو عن أحد المتساويين في الذنب دون الآخر؛ لأنه لا تفاوت في فضله وعدله»، فخطأ فاحش مخالف للكتاب والسنة، وتحكم على الله تعالى في مقام الإرادة والمشيئة، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الْفَضْلَ بِيَدِ اللَّهِ يُؤْتِيهِ مَنْ يَشَاءُ﴾ [آل عمران: ٧٣]. وحاصل المرام في هذا المقام أن أمره سبحانه بالنسبة إلى عباده لا يخلو عن عدله وفضله على وفق مراده مع أنه قد ورد في حديث روي موقوفا ومرفوعا: ((لو أن الله عذب أهل سماواته وأهل أرضه عذبهم وهو غير ظالم لهم، ولو رحمهم كانت رحمته خيرا لهم من أعمالهم)). رواه أحمد وأبو داود وابن ماجه. (١) سنن أبي داود، كتاب السنة، باب في القدر، ٢٩٨/٤، حديث: ٤٦٩٩.
And He may punish for sin, as an act of justice from Him, and He may pardon, as an act of grace from Him. And He may punish for sin, i.e., to the extent that the servant deserves, without increase of punishment, as an act of justice from Him, as He informed about it in His Book by His saying, the Most High: 'Whoever comes with a good deed, for him are ten like it; and whoever comes with an evil deed, he is not recompensed except the like of it, and they will not be wronged' [Al-An'am 6:160], i.e., by reduction of reward or increase of punishment. And He may pardon, i.e., the evil deed, as an act of grace from Him, whether it be through intercession or without it, due to His saying, the Blessed and Most High: 'And whatever misfortune befalls you, it is because of what your hands have earned, and He pardons much' [Ash-Shura 42:30], and due to His saying, the Most High: 'And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [An-Nisa 4:48], i.e., what is less than shirk, small or great, for whom He desires forgiveness, as a grace. The summary is that the tenfold increase is general, but the increase beyond that is specific, and all is pure grace and pure mercy. And perhaps the increase occurs due to the difference in stations of the people of worship, or due to the mere attachment of will to what has preceded for them of the care of happiness. As for the saying of a commentator: 'He cannot give of reward to one of two equals in worship and certainty more than He gives the other, nor pardon one of two equals in sin without the other, because there is no disparity in His grace and justice'—it is a grievous error, contrary to the Book and the Sunnah, and an arbitrary ruling over Allah, the Most High, in the station of will and volition. And Allah, the Most High, has said: 'Indeed, grace is in the hand of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills' [Al-i-Imran 3:73]. And the purport of the desired matter in this station is that His command, the Exalted, with respect to His servants is not devoid of His justice and His grace, in accordance with His will. Moreover, it has been reported in a hadith narrated as both mauquf and marfu': 'If Allah were to punish the inhabitants of His heavens and the inhabitants of His earth, He would punish them and He is not unjust to them, and if He were to have mercy on them, His mercy would be better for them than their deeds.' Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Majah. (1) Sunan Abi Dawud, Kitab as-Sunnah, Bab fi al-Qadr, 4/298, Hadith 4699.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a foundational creedal statement regarding God's punishment and forgiveness. The commentator begins by clarifying that when God punishes a sin, He does so as an act of justice ('adl), meaning He gives exactly what the servant deserves—no more. He supports this with Qur'an 6:160, which promises ten rewards for a good deed but only the exact equivalent for an evil deed, implying that punishment is perfectly proportionate and never excessive. Then he explains that when God forgives, it is an act of grace (fadl), and this forgiveness may come with or without intercession, citing Qur'an 42:30 and 4:48 to show that God pardons many sins, including major ones, purely out of His favor. The commentator then synthesizes: the tenfold reward is general, but any additional increase is specific and purely grace, not owed. He further notes that such increase may be due to the varying spiritual stations of the worshippers or to God's sheer will. Next, he refutes a mistaken commentator who claimed that God cannot differentiate among equal individuals in reward or forgiveness because that would imply disparity in His grace or justice. The author labels this view a 'grievous error' contrary to revelation, since God's will is sovereign, as Qur'an 3:73 states. He concludes that God's dealings with His servants always combine justice and grace according to His will, and he reinforces this with a hadith: even if God punished all creatures, He would not be unjust, and if He showed mercy, that mercy would surpass their deeds.

Key Terms
عدل
عقاب
استحقاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God might punish sinners more than they deserve due to His power.
Correction: The passage clarifies that punishment is 'بلا زيادة عقوبة' (without increase), consistent with His justice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'عدل' (justice) mean in the context of punishment?
A) God punishes every sin without exception.
B) The punishment is exactly what the servant deserves, without increase.
C) Punishment is only for major sins.
D) Punishment is always less than what is deserved.

Key Takeaway
God's punishment is an act of perfect justice, giving exactly what is deserved without any excess.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that God's punishment will be exactly what you deserve and no more? How does that certainty shape your attitude toward repentance and hope in His mercy?
?
If you knew that every good deed you do will be multiplied tenfold in reward, would that change how you spend your time today? What one small good deed can you commit to doing right now?
?
Are you ever tempted to think that God's punishment is harsher than necessary? Reflect on the verse 'and they will not be wronged' – does this settle your heart about His justice, or does it raise a deeper question about your own sense of fairness?

Forgiveness as Grace and Divine Sovereignty
Explanation of forgiveness as grace and refutation of error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's forgiveness is an act of grace (fadl) and that He has absolute sovereignty to bestow or withhold it as He wills, refuting the notion that He must treat equals equally.

Core Idea
God's forgiveness is pure grace; He is free to give or withhold as He wills.

After establishing punishment as justice, the commentator turns to forgiveness. He explains that when God pardons, He does so as an act of grace, not obligation. This lesson explores the concept of fadl, the Quranic proofs, and a refutation of those who wrongly limit God's freedom in bestowing grace.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on forgiveness
Read the Arabic passage about forgiveness (starting from 'وقد يعفو') and its translation. Note the key term 'فضل' (grace).
The passage distinguishes forgiveness from punishment: the latter is justice, the former is grace.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Find the two verses cited (42:30 and 4:48) and understand how they support forgiveness as grace, even for major sins.
Verse 4:48 specifies that God forgives 'what is less than shirk' for whom He wills.
3
Understand the synthesis about reward
The commentator says the tenfold reward is general, but additional increase is specific. Reflect on why this shows grace.
The base reward is justice; any extra is pure grace.
4
Analyze the refutation
Read the refutation of the commentator who claimed God cannot differentiate among equals. Identify the error and the counter-evidence from Quran 3:73.
The error is limiting God's will; the response affirms divine sovereignty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God must treat all equal individuals equally in reward and forgiveness because His justice and grace are uniform.
Correction: The passage refutes this by asserting God's absolute sovereignty: He gives grace to whom He wills, as He says in Quran 3:73.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the commentator's refutation of the erroneous view?
A) The hadith about punishment and mercy.
B) The verse 'Indeed, grace is in the hand of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills.'
C) The principle that God's justice forbids differentiation.
D) The idea that intercession is required for forgiveness.

Key Takeaway
God's forgiveness is an act of grace that He bestows according to His will, not constrained by any necessity of equal treatment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that your good deeds place God in your debt, expecting a guaranteed reward? How does the truth that even your best deeds are only met with justice (the tenfold increase) while any extra is pure grace change your heart about relying on your own actions? Will you today stop bargaining with Allah and instead ask for His grace with humility?
?
When you see someone who sins openly yet receives blessings or ease from Allah, do you feel a pang of injustice? How does this lesson's emphasis on Allah's absolute freedom to give or withhold grace challenge your instinct to compare? What would it look like for you to truly accept that His giving is not based on your personal sense of fairness?
?
The hadith says: 'If Allah were to punish you, He would not be unjust; if He shows mercy, it is better than your deeds.' Does this truth make you more hopeful or more fearful? In what area of your life are you relying on your own goodness instead of throwing yourself entirely upon His mercy? What one concrete change can you make today to shift your trust from your deeds to His grace?

Divine Guidance and Misguidance: Fadl and Adl
Definition of divine guidance as grace and misguidance as justice, with explanation of khidhlan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of divine guidance and misguidance, that guidance is a grace and misguidance is justice, and the meaning of khidhlan (abandonment).

Core Idea
God's guidance is grace; His misguidance is justice, never arbitrary.

This lesson explains a foundational belief in Sunni Islam: that Allah's actions in guiding or leading astray are always perfectly just and gracious. The passage from Imam al-A'zam defines these terms and addresses a common misunderstanding about divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage combines definition, commentary, and a Quranic verse.
2
Identify the definitions
Find where the passage defines guidance (هداية) as grace (فضل) and misguidance (ضلال) as justice (عدل). Note how it explains 'leading astray' as 'abandonment' (خذلان).
3
Understand khidhlan and tawfiq
The passage says khidhlan is not granting tawfiq (success) to the servant. Ask yourself: Why is this considered just?
The commentary clarifies that nothing is obligatory upon Allah.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verse from al-An'am 125. How does it illustrate the effects of divine guidance and misguidance?
The verse describes physical and spiritual states.
5
Note the sectarian disagreement
The passage ends by mentioning the Mu'tazila. Reflect on why they might disagree with this doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والله تعالى يهدي من يشاء فضلاً منه ويضل من يشاء عدلاً منه، وإضلاله خذلانه وتفسير الخذلان أن لا يوفق العبد إلى ما يرضاه منه، وهو عدل منه. والله تعالى يهدي من يشاء أي إلى الإيمان والطاعة فضلاً منه أي يجعله مظهر جماله ومحل ثوابه ويضل من يشاء أي بالكفر والمعصية عدلاً منه أي يجعله مظهر جلاله وموضع عقابه ثم هدايته وتوفيقه وإحسانه، وهذه جملة مطوية معلومة القضية، ولذا لم يتعرض له الإمام واكتفى بذكر ما فيه من اختلاف بعض الأنام حيث قال: (وإضلاله خذلانه أي عدم نصرته في مقام تحقيقه ومرام تصديقه. وتفسير الخذلان أن لا يوفّق العبد أي لا يحمله إلى ما يرضاه منه أي على ما يحبه من الإيمان والإحسان ويكون سببا لرضى الرب عن العبد وهو أي الخذلان وعدم رضاه عنه عدل منه إذ لا يجب عليه شيء لغيره، وقد وضع الشيء في موضعه كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَمَنْ يُرِدِ اللهُ أَنْ يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرَهُ لِلْإِسْلَامِ وَمَنْ يُرِدْ أَنْ يُضِلَّهُ يَجْعَلْ صَدْرَهُ ضَيِّقًا حَرَجًا كَأَنَّمَا يَصَّعَدُ فِي السَّمَاءِ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٢٥]. وكذا عقوبة المخذول على المعصية أي عدل منه في نظر أرباب العقول وأصحاب النقول. وفي المسألة خلاف المعتزلة.
And Allah Most High guides whom He wills as a grace from Him, and leads astray whom He wills as a justice from Him. And His leading astray is His abandonment (khidhlan), and the interpretation of abandonment is that He does not grant success (tawfiq) to the servant to what pleases Him from him, and it is justice from Him. And Allah Most High guides whom He wills, that is, to faith and obedience, as a grace from Him, that is, He makes him a manifestation of His beauty and a place of His reward; and leads astray whom He wills, that is, to disbelief and disobedience, as a justice from Him, that is, He makes him a manifestation of His majesty and a place of His punishment. Then His guidance, success, and beneficence are a hidden matter known in its entirety; therefore the Imam did not address it and sufficed with mentioning what difference of opinion concerning it occurs among some people, where he said: “And His leading astray is His abandonment, that is, His not granting victory in the station of its realization and the aim of its confirmation. And the interpretation of abandonment is that He does not grant success (tawfiq) to the servant,” that is, He does not impel him to what pleases Him from him, that is, to what He loves of faith and beneficence, which becomes a cause for the Lord's pleasure with the servant. “And it” – that is, abandonment and His displeasure with him – “is justice from Him, for nothing is obligatory upon Him for another, and He has placed the thing in its proper place, as Allah Most High said: 'So whoever Allah intends to guide, He expands his breast to Islam; and whoever He intends to lead astray, He makes his breast tight and constricted, as if he were ascending into the sky' [al-An'am 125].” Likewise, punishment of the abandoned one for disobedience is justice from Him in the view of possessors of intellect and transmitted knowledge. And there is disagreement with the Mu'tazila on this matter.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage defines the Islamic doctrine of divine guidance and misguidance. It begins by stating that Allah guides whom He wills as a grace (fadl) and leads astray whom He wills as justice (adl). The author then explains that 'leading astray' is actually khidhlan (abandonment), interpreted as Allah not granting tawfiq (success) to the servant to do what pleases Him. This is described as justice, because nothing is owed by Allah to any creature. The commentary expands on the initial statement, explaining that guidance to faith is a manifestation of Allah's beauty and reward, while misguidance to disbelief is a manifestation of His majesty and punishment. The commentator notes that the Imam (al-A'zam) did not elaborate on the hidden wisdom of guidance and success, but only mentioned the point of disagreement among some people. The passage then quotes the Qur'anic verse from al-An'am 125, which describes the physical and spiritual effects of divine guidance and misguidance. Finally, it asserts that punishment of the abandoned one for disobedience is also justice, and notes that the Mu'tazila disagree with this position.

Key Terms
الهداية (guidance)
الضلال (misguidance)
الفضل (grace)
العدل (justice)
الخذلان (abandonment)
التوفيق (success/granting of ability)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God's misguidance is unjust or arbitrary.
Correction: The passage clarifies that misguidance is always just, as it is a form of abandonment (khidhlan) and Allah places everything in its proper place.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator say about the interpretation of khidhlan (abandonment)?
A) It is Allah's arbitrary punishment without cause.
B) It means Allah does not grant the servant success to what pleases Him, and it is justice.
C) It means Allah forces the servant into disbelief.
D) It is a temporary state that may change.

Key Takeaway
Guidance is a grace from Allah, and misguidance is His justice, accomplished through abandonment (khidhlan), which means withholding tawfiq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your faith is solely by Allah's grace (fadl) and not your merit, how does that crush your pride in your own obedience? Will you thank Him today as though your every good deed is a gift?
?
When you see someone rejecting faith, do you recognize that their state is under Allah's justice (adl) and not mere bad luck? How should that change your condescension or despair toward them?
?
Have you felt spiritually 'abandoned' in your efforts to worship? Understanding khidhlan as the withholding of tawfiq, will you now plead for tawfiq rather than blame yourself or Allah? What specific step will you take to seek His help?

Persian for Allah's Attributes Except the Hand
The author rules on using Persian for certain attributes of Allah, except for 'al-yad'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on using Persian (or non-Arabic) for Allah's attributes, and the specific exception for the attribute of the Hand (al-yad).

Core Idea
Persian for Allah's attributes is allowed except for 'al-yad', which must stay in Arabic.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary clarifies a nuanced issue: which of Allah's attributes may be expressed in Persian? While most ambiguous attributes like the Face and Eye can be rendered in other languages, the Hand is strictly reserved for its Quranic and Sunnah phrasing. The lesson explains the reasoning and the importance of avoiding anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the overall ruling and exception.
Pay attention to variant readings in parentheses.
2
Identify the general rule and the exception
Locate where the text states that Persian is permissible for Allah's attributes, and then the specific exception for 'al-yad'.
The exception is introduced by 'sawa al-yad'.
3
Understand why 'al-yad' is exceptional
Consider the reason given: it must be expressed only according to the phrasing that came in the Book and Sunnah, implying a special reverence for this attribute.
This does not deny the attribute, but restricts its linguistic expression.
4
See the application for 'al-wajh'
Note the example of 'ruwi-yi Khuda' for the Face of Allah, and the condition of negating tashbih and takyif.
This shows how the general permission is applied with theological safeguards.
5
Reflect on the principle of avoiding tashbih and takyif
Understand that all expressions of Allah's attributes, whether in Arabic or Persian, must be free from anthropomorphism and modality.
This is a key principle in Sunni kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل ما وفي نسخة: 'وكل شيء' ذكره العلماء (بالفارسية) أي بغير العبارة العربية من صفات الله (تعالى أي المتشابهة كالوجه والقدم والعين. وفي نسخة: 'من صفات الباري' عزت أسماؤه أي غلبت على الأفهام وتعالت صفاته أي ارتفعت عن الأوهام فجائز القول به أي بأن نتبعهم في التعبير عن أسمائه وصفاته حسب ما ذكره العلماء باختلاف لغاته سوى اليد (بالفارسية أي فإنه لا يجوز تعبيرها بالفارسية كما في نسخة: أي بغير عبارة وردت في الكتاب والسنة، ومفهومه أنه يجوز للعلماء وغيرهم أن يعبروا في صفته ونعته بذكر اليد ونحوها على وفق ما ورد بها كما يقال بيده أزمة التحقيق، والله ولي التوفيق. ويتفرع على الحصر المذكور بالوجه المسطور قوله : ويجوز أن يقال: «بروى خدا» بضم الراء وسكون الواو أي وجه الله بلا تشبيه ولا كيفية أي مقرونا بنفي التشبيه والكيفية من صدر
And everything (and in a copy: 'and every thing') that the scholars mentioned (in Persian) i.e., in other than the Arabic phrase, from the attributes of Allah (Exalted, i.e., the ambiguous like the Face, the Foot, and the Eye. And in a copy: 'from the attributes of the Creator')—may His names be mighty, i.e., they dominate the intellects, and His attributes be exalted, i.e., they are elevated above imaginations—then it is permissible to say it, i.e., that we follow them in expression of His names and attributes according to what the scholars mentioned in different languages, except for 'al-yad' (the hand) (in Persian, i.e., it is not permissible to express it in Persian, as in a copy: i.e., in other than a phrase that came in the Book and the Sunnah). And its understanding is that it is permissible for scholars and others to express in His attribute and description by mentioning 'al-yad' and the like according to what has come, as it is said: 'In His hand is the grip of verification.' And Allah is the Grantor of success. And there branches from the aforementioned restriction the statement: And it is permissible to say: 'ruwi-yi Khuda' (with dammah on the ra' and sukun on the waw), i.e., the Face of Allah, without tashbih or takyif, i.e., accompanied by negation of tashbih and takyif from the [chest?].
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on using Persian (or non-Arabic) terms for Allah's attributes. It begins by stating that whatever scholars have mentioned in Persian, aside from Arabic, concerning Allah's attributes—specifically the ambiguous (mutashabih) attributes like the Face, Foot, and Eye—is permissible to say, following the scholars' usage in various languages. However, there is an explicit exception: the attribute 'al-yad' (the hand) must not be expressed in Persian; it should only be used according to the phrasing that appears in the Quran and Sunnah. The passage further explains that one may still affirm the hand in Arabic phrases like 'In His hand is the grip of verification.' After establishing this exception, the text states that it is permissible to say 'ruwi-yi Khuda' (face of God) in Persian, with the condition of negating any anthropomorphism (tashbih) and modality (kayfiyyah). This ruling is derived from the same principle that allows using Persian for other attributes while strictly following transmitted expressions for 'al-yad'.

Key Terms

الفارسية
الصفات المتشابهة
الوجه
التشبيه
الكيفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The exception for 'al-yad' means that the attribute of the Hand is denied or not real.
Correction: The exception is only about linguistic expression: 'al-yad' must be expressed in Arabic scriptural forms, but the attribute itself is affirmed as it came in revelation.

Checkpoint
Which attribute of Allah is specifically prohibited from being expressed in Persian according to this passage?
A) The Face (al-wajh)
B) The Foot (al-qadam)
C) The Hand (al-yad)
D) The Eye (al-ayn)

Key Takeaway
The use of Persian for Allah's attributes is generally permissible for ambiguous attributes like the Face, but the Hand must be expressed only in the original Arabic scriptural forms, and all such expressions must be accompanied by denying anthropomorphism and modality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about Allah's attributes, do you ever catch yourself forming mental images of a hand or face that resemble yours? How does the ruling in this lesson—that even the language must be scripturally precise—guard your tongue and heart from such slips? Commit today to only using the exact words of revelation when mentioning the Hand of Allah, and to reminding yourself that 'there is nothing like unto Him'.
?
This lesson shows that even the language we use for Allah is regulated by revelation, down to the choice of Arabic versus Persian. In your daily conversations, do you pay attention to the words you use about Allah, or do you speak casually? Which attribute are you most likely to describe in your own words rather than the Quranic phrasing? Resolve to look up the exact verse for that attribute and use it in your next supplication.
?
The permission to use Persian for some attributes shows that Islam accommodates other languages without compromising the sacred text. Are you tempted to rely solely on translations and neglect the original Arabic? What does your choice say about your reverence for the divine speech? Ask yourself: Am I striving to understand the Arabic of the Quran more deeply, or am I content with a secondhand understanding?
